### Post by nbcthreat on 2005-12-11
If you're  like a lot of folks on here you have a cutting-edge system that spends most of its time idling on a blank screen or running a cool screensaver. It's possibel to donate your spare cycles to cancer and other medical research using Folding@Home.

[http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Folding_at_home](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Folding_at_home)

There are a couple of Ubuntu teams, but we're in the process of attempting to unify behind the team with the most points. Here's the link.

[http://fah-web.stanford.edu/cgi-bin/main.py?qtype=teampage&teamnum=45104](http://fah-web.stanford.edu/cgi-bin/main.py?qtype=teampage&teamnum=45104)

And here's the wiki page.

[https://wiki.ubuntu.com/FoldingAtHomeTeamUbuntu?highlight=%28folding%29](https://wiki.ubuntu.com/FoldingAtHomeTeamUbuntu?highlight=%28folding%29)

Also, here's a great post on Hackaday about tips for competitive folding.

[http://www.hackaday.com/entry/1234000673058540/](http://www.hackaday.com/entry/1234000673058540/)

Come join the team and have some competitive geeky fun while helping cure diseases! What could be better?

---

### Post by erikpiper on 2005-12-11
How well does it work with systems that have a (relatively) low uptime? As in, my nice machine is a dual booting gamer- can it start itself automatically? Any bugs?

---

### Post by Zelut on 2005-12-11
It can start itself automagally at boot on either side (Linux or Windows).  I've got a personal team (24 machines) running on both platforms and I haven't seen any problems.

I'd join the team but I've already put so much work into my own team :)

### Post by nbcthreat on 2005-12-12

The only reason I don't run it while I'm working on my laptop at work is that it means that the laptop gets hot and the fan runs full-time which is annoying. I run it on everythine else.

### Post by ned.b on 2005-12-27
[QUOTE=Rinzwind]*Reporting as a new recruit*

My P4 3.0 now running folding@home for team 45104 :)
(as soon as I find out how to add to a team :) )[/QUOTE]

Welcome! :-)

When you first run the client on a box you have the option to specify a team; if you need ammend any of the details you first entered then start the client with the -config switch.  For example from the directory you run your client from type: 

 ./FAH502-Linux.exe -config

### Post by nbcthreat on 2005-12-27
I've got my P4 2.4 HT at home running 2 clients. I have a small P3 700 at home, and my Pentium M laptop here at work when I'm gone. I had had my two unused P4 laptops at work running for a while, but it was a hassle because I only have one net connection here in the office and had to keep moving the cable around to upload work units. Now that I feel the heat, I've got them plugged in in another office so they don't require maintenance. That's two more P4 cores. I should be rocking.

---

### Post by nbcthreat on 2005-12-27
Oh, and by the by. On Windows, the client is set up to run super-nice and not interfere at all with what you're doing. On Linux, I don't know what the deal is. It does seem to slow down my UI a bit when I have my folding clients running on my box at home, so I started running them with "nice" and it seems to make it more responsive. Something you might try if your box is feeling sluggish while you're folding in the background.

```
nice ./FAH5*
```

---

### Post by nbcthreat on 2005-12-27
[QUOTE=Swab]Is there an advantage to running 2 clients on one CPU?[/QUOTE]

Well, there's some debate on the subject. But the tweaking article I link to at the beginning of the thread and in the wiki suggests that running two clients on a hyperthreading chip will accomplish more points per hour overall. Check out hyperthreading on wikipedia.

[http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hyperthreading]("http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hyperthreading")

---

### Post by ned.b on 2005-12-28
[QUOTE=Rinzwind]I'm still on 0 according to the stats-page :([/QUOTE]

Rinzwind are you overclocked?

"Overclocking
... If your machine is heavily OC’d and you are seeing weird stats reported on the Team stats page i.e. 5 work units returned but 5 points granted, you probably are seeing early work ends (EWEs). These are where the simulation reached a point where it could not continue. This is usually caused by an unstable OC, though not always. If this is the case you should turn your OC down a bit to lend stability to the system. "

[http://www.hackaday.com/entry/1234000673058540/](http://www.hackaday.com/entry/1234000673058540/)

### Post by Swab on 2005-12-29
So I was thinking we could post a plea for more folders into each of the non-english Ubuntu forums.

We'd need to come up with our spiel in English then have it translated into Chinese, Dutch, German, Finnish, French, Italian, Polish, and Portugese.

Thoughts?

Edit: This is taken from a posting on the folding@home forums:

> Most of your computer&#8217;s computing power goes unused. For example, surfing the net, writing essays, and listening to mp3&#8217;s uses between 5 &#8211; 30% of your computer&#8217;s resources. The rest simply goes wasted. By simply downloading the Folding@home program and letting it run, you can help save lives. The program doesn&#8217;t affect your computer&#8217;s performance at all. It unobtrusively uses your computers wasted power to study protein misfolding.

The Folding@home project is dedicated to help study the causes of Alzheimer's, Mad Cow (BSE), CJD, ALS, and Parkinson's disease. By doing this, the project hopes that its contribution to understanding the underlying causes of these horrible diseases will help in the search to find a cure or vaccine. In fact, they are already helping. Folding@home is the only distributed computing project that has produced significant results and published them in a major scientific journal such as Nature.

Running the program doesn&#8217;t cost you anything. It turns off when you turn off your computer and it only uses the CPU cycles that you are not using. So, when you run a game that needs 100% of your computer&#8217;s resources, you&#8217;ll have 100% of your computer&#8217;s resources.

Folding@home is a non-profit project put out by researchers at Stanford University. All information produced by the project is made available to others free of charge.

Go to: folding.stanford.edu to dowload the client or for more information.

We could add on something about TeamUbuntu at the end.

---

### Post by chiefofthejojos on 2006-01-15

---

### Post by red_Marvin on 2006-01-15
Folding@home runs on your spare cycles, which is the ones that otherwise wouldn't
be used, which is the most of them if the computer is idle
You could always open up gnome-system-monitor (or equivalent) and checking it's
nice value, if it's zero or higher you got no problems then it runs "in the background".

---

### Post by mstlyevil on 2006-01-15
[QUOTE=chiefofthejojos]I'm a little nervous about my system here.  It's an AMD Sempron 2200+ and Folding@Home always makes it run at 100% CPU, is this normal/safe?[/QUOTE]

Your CPU is supposed to run at 100% with Folding@Home. That is what the program does is it uses otherwise idle CPU cycles. The program is structured so that when you use your computer, the F@H processes run in the background so you do not have a performance hit. Whatever you are deoing has first priority so the program either slows or pauses until you are done and then resumes. 100% CPU ususage means that it is working correctly.

---

### Post by ned.b on 2006-01-25
ATTENTION SMP/HYPERTHREADING CPU USERS!

Running 2 cores?  Have you assumed you are automatically using Hyperthreading/SMP on your shiny new install of Breezy? Read on...

If you click Applications/System Tools/ System Monitor/Resources do you see 2 CPU entries?  If so bravo and you can probably ignore the following blurb.  If not then check out Poofy's guide to selecting the right kernel for your machine:

[http://www.ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=85917](http://www.ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=85917)

When I did this ooh absolutely ages ago (I definately haven't been running on 386 kernels for the last couple of months - no way ;) )  I had a problem - my machine locked up totally, it seems my Belkin wireless adapter does not support SMP kernels - yet, but maybe a few of you can squeeze some extra work units out and boost TeamUbuntu's performance...

---

### Post by nbcthreat on 2006-01-25
I'm using hyperthreading on a few machines. My home system is a P4 with HT and I have two instances of folding running on that.

Today, though, I installed 4 instances of folding on one machine... my secret weapon (big grin).

---

### Post by nbcthreat on 2006-01-25
The competitive folding article in the wiki and in the first post describes how to optimize for HT. It's a must-read for all team ubuntu members. I noticed that our points per unit hav been dropping, people must not be optimizing.

### Post by Grey on 2006-01-29
I have it running on my laptop.  (Not for this team though, sorry guys).  I have a Pentium M 1.73GHz, with CPU scaling enabled of course.  I'm not sure if there's a hit on my battery life, as I haven't done any extensive testing on that.  But the CPU stays at 800MHz with F@H running.  Which is good enough for me.  When the CPU jumps to 1.73GHz for another app, it takes about a second longer to drop down to 800MHz again when I am done with it... but it does a good job.

### Post by ndhskp on 2006-02-26

### Post by mjwood0 on 2006-02-26
Okay.  I answered my own question.

To reconfigure Folding@Home when running as a daemon:

1. Stop the service
```
sudo /etc/init.d/foldingathome stop
```

2. Run the same command the service runs, specifing the -configonly option.  For me, this is /opt/foldingathome/config/FAH502-Linux.exe
```
sudo /opt/foldingathome/config/FAH502-Linux.exe -configonly
```

3. Select the options you want.  Your current values show up as defaults so you shouldn't have to do anything but hit enter if you don't want to change them.

4. When you are done, restart the service.
```
sudo /etc/init.d/foldingathome start
```

Worked fine for me!  Good luck all!

---

### Post by mjwood0 on 2006-02-26
[QUOTE=xhie]And shutting it down? Do I have to do something to get it to save what its doing or will it just take care of itself when I shutdown?[/QUOTE]

As others have said, no.  You don't have to.  FAH periodically saves it's work.  By default, this setting is 15 minutes.  Therefore, if you start your computer and shut it down after less than 15 minutes, you loose all work for that time.

For this reason, I changed my default to 5 minute saves.  This way, since I run on a laptop, when I'm going during the day and my computer is turning on and off, I still get credit for most of my CPU's work.

Something to think about if you shutdown frequently.

---

### Post by ndhskp on 2006-03-03
[quote=Swab]Well, I'm sure I just changed one line in /etc/init.d/foldingathome 

executable=FAH502-Linux.exe

to

executable=FAH502-Linux.exe -advmethods

But when I try that now, it doesn;t work.

I'm not actually using the script at the moment as I've been trying out 504 beta.. which includes an option in the setup for persistent -advmethods .... so maybe the script just needs to be modified to use the beta client...[/quote]Here's how I did it.  I opened both scripts in Gedit and replaced all instance's of **"FAH502-Linux.exe"** with **"FAH504-Linux.exe"**.  This will allow you to use the beta client with the script and saying yes to changing advance option allows you to say yes to persistent -advmethods.  So that's what i'm running right now the beta 5.04 client.  Cheers

---

### Post by Swab on 2006-03-03

So that's what i'm running right now the beta 5.04 client.  Cheers[/QUOTE]

### Post by ndhskp on 2006-03-29
[quote=xmastree]Well, I installed some this morning, but not all as yet. I had more inportant stuff to do.
I'll do the rest by the end of the week.

For those interested, the hot server is built into an old desktop case, so it looks old on the outside, but 'under the hood' it's pretty quick. 8) 


Click the pic for the story behind it.

Like I said though, it's rather warm so I'll leave F@H off it.[/quote]If your PCI slots will remain empty then drill and place a fan blowhole on top of the case over the PCI slots and open up some holes in the front thereby drawing the air in over the motherboard.  By the time it gets to the PCI blowhole it will be pretty warm.  Open up a hole by the cpu as well.  And make it a 120mm fan size.

---

### Post by ndhskp on 2006-03-29
[quote=Hygelac]I would be very interested in that cooling advice.  I have a Pentium III (You may have noticed that I manage to get a lot of old machines) that I could probably run FAH on.  The only problem with it is that it heats up very fast when working at full capacity (about 75°C after about an hour!).  If I could keep it cool I might be able to get somewhere with it.  It's nearly obsolete though, so I guess it doesn't really matter that much.[/quote]Make sure it's clean, get rid of all dust and other crap.  Check fans for any obstructions.  Reseat all connectors and bunch up and tie cables out of the way of the airflow.  Get rid of unnecessary PCI cards as well as CD-ROM drives and floppy dives if you don't ever use them.  Don't block vents, keep at least 1 inch of space clear around vents if not more.

Don't run computers in a closed cabinet or similar funiture.  Try air-conditioning your home if you can afford to do it.  If all else fails remove the cpu fan and clean the old thermal paste off the cpu and fan cooling block untill both are shiny again and apply new thermal paste.  I use Arctic Silver thermal paste myself.  Maybe consider getting a new cpu cooling block and fan while your at it.

Other things to consider are case design and how it routes air flow.  Power supplys that are going bad can cause big heat buildups as well.  Modern video cards are really bad heat generaters.  This should get you and other people thinking.

---

### Post by ndhskp on 2006-04-05
[quote=xmastree]Of course I did. How else am I expected to climb up the ladder?[/quote]The machine ID is only a problem on "multi-core" and "multi-cpu" and "hyperthreaded" systems.  Totally separate machines can have the same machine ID and all machines should have the same username for that paticular user.  Also xmastree if you have a firewall or router check your firewall or router for the proper port holes.

### Post by ndhskp on 2006-04-07

### Post by jpkotta on 2006-04-08
If you used the installer and init script that I wrote (the one on the wiki), you can easily make a cron job to turn it on and off at set times.  Say you want it to stop at midnight and start at 8:00 every morning.  Run ```
sudo crontab -e
``` and an editor should pop up, and you can add the following lines
```
0 8 * * * /etc/init.d/foldingathome start
0 0 * * * /etc/init.d/foldingathome stop
```
The format is minute, hour, day, month, day of the week, command.  * means all.

So, on april 7th it reached 17%, but on april 8th it started over...

:confused:

I presume the timestamps are GMT, since it's currently at 15% and it's 09:47 here, or 01:47 GMT.

Why is it restarting, and how can i stop it?[/QUOTE]


If the machines are overclocked... or are just overheating then they may produce errors resulting in them having to start over again.

### Post by drizek on 2006-04-09
If it does that then your overclock is too high. The beta client shouldnt be a problem, just make sure you lower your clockspeed. IF you want to see if your OC is stable try using a program called prime95. If it runs for a day or two straight without errors then you know that it is OK.

### Post by drizek on 2006-04-27
The windows version works just fine here.

---

### Post by jpkotta on 2006-04-27
[QUOTE=drizek]The windows version works just fine here.

Are you using the console version and did you set it to autostart?[/QUOTE]

Yeah, console version is the way to go on all OSes.  This is really easy to do in Windows:

[LIST=1]
[*]Download the console client.
[*]Create a folder like C:\foldingathome and move it there.
[*]Start a terminal (cmd.exe) and cd to the folder.
[*]Run "FAH....exe -configonly".
[*]Set the options as you like, but make sure to set it up as a service.
[*]You can start it immediately from the services tool (buried somewhere in the Control Panel).
[/LIST]

It starts automatically on boot when installed as a service.

---

### Post by asimon on 2006-06-17
[QUOTE=flankker]

Find your name at [TeamUbuntu individual User List](http://folding.extremeoverclocking.com/user_list.php?s=&t=45104), your total work units are in the last column. Also the F@H client itself outputs your total work units when it submits a finished one.

---

### Post by flankker on 2006-06-17
[QUOTE=asimon]Find your name at [TeamUbuntu individual User List](http://folding.extremeoverclocking.com/user_list.php?s=&t=45104), your total work units are in the last column. Also the F@H client itself outputs your total work units when it submits a finished one.[/QUOTE]

thanx for the reply, but what i meant was how do i know what percentage of a work unit ive already done? is this possible at all?

---

### Post by asimon on 2006-06-17
[QUOTE=flankker]thanx for the reply, but what i meant was how do i know what percentage of a work unit ive already done? is this possible at all?[/QUOTE]
Yes, in the directory where you installed F@H, you'll find a file named 'unitinfo.txt'. It contains the progress. For example mine currently is
```

$ cat ~/FAH/unitinfo.txt
Current Work Unit
-----------------
Name: p2095_Protein
Download time: June 15 14:39:57
Due time: August 3 14:39:57
Progress: 52%  [|||||_____]

```
The logfile 'FAHlog.txt' also contains the percentage info.

---

### Post by flankker on 2006-06-17
[QUOTE=asimon]Yes, in the directory where you installed F@H, you'll find a file named 'unitinfo.txt'. It contains the progress. For example mine currently is
```

$ cat ~/FAH/unitinfo.txt
Current Work Unit
-----------------
Name: p2095_Protein
Download time: June 15 14:39:57
Due time: August 3 14:39:57
Progress: 52%  [|||||_____]

```
The logfile 'FAHlog.txt' also contains the percentage info.[/QUOTE]

thanx a lot, that is exactly what i was looking for.

### Post by msak007 on 2006-06-25
I just signed up a week ago, and I'm already 304922 out of 557410. Woot! :) Anyway I'm not sure if this has been mentioned before (I tried to search within the post and couldn't find anything), but for all you fellow Kubuntu users there's a KDE kicker applet for folding@home. It has a progress bar so you can see how far along it is, and right-clicking on it gives you access to all your stats and the option to stop / start folding. You can find it and more info about it [here]("http://www.kde-apps.org/content/show.php?content=10213")  at the kde-apps web site. I use it and it's been working great for me!

### Post by o_fortuna on 2006-06-26
I was gone for a month, and I only fell back a few places. Ha! Now I'm back.

> So just how does the scoring work that this has happened?
Some WUs are worth way more than others. Some that I've had recently have been 400-point WUs, and some have been just 60-pointers. So, five 60-point WUs isn't as good as on 400-point WU.

The currently "active" WUs, and their point values, are here: [http://vspx27.stanford.edu/psummary.html]("http://vspx27.stanford.edu/psummary.html")

---

### Post by T313C0mun1s7 on 2006-06-26
[quote=o_fortuna]Some WUs are worth way more than others. Some that I've had recently have been 400-point WUs, and some have been just 60-pointers. So, five 60-point WUs isn't as good as on 400-point WU.

The currently "active" WUs, and their point values, are here: [http://vspx27.stanford.edu/psummary.html]("http://vspx27.stanford.edu/psummary.html")[/quote]                                                 
Thank you for the quick reply. I remember something during the setup about allowing for WUs that take more than 5Mb or RAM (I think that is what it was) and the default was no. I guess by answering yes to that question, since I have plenty of RAM available, I opened myself up to getting WUs of higher value.

This brings up a interesting question. If the default is no (and so one could assume that will be the answer most people will select) then as a competitive group should we encourage those people with larger amounts of (spare) RAM to change this option to yes? If I am running a basic workstation with 1Gb or more of RAM I think I can afford to give a little to the project. Of course there are times when this might not be a good idea. Like if I have 8Gb of RAM but I have the client running on a production database server (which I wouldn't) It is most likely best to leave the RAM available for the database.

### Post by T313C0mun1s7 on 2006-07-02
First off, I found my rogue client and got it fixed.

Instructions - Hmm, I am not an expert but I can give some really good links and how I did it.

[A Complete Guide to Using FINSTALL for NEWbies]("http://fahwiki.net/index.php/A_Complete_Guide_to_Using_FINSTALL_for_NEWbies")

This is a quickstart on how I did it. For me this worked well, automatically created everything I needed, and set up one client per CPU.

```

cd ~
mkdir folding
cd folding
wget http://www.stanford.edu/group/pandegroup/release/FAH502-Linux.exe
chmod +x FAH502-Linux.exe
./FAH502-Linux.exe
``` 
It will then start the setup script and you are off. Here are a couple more hints to make things go smoother:[LIST=1]
[*]Pick a username before you start, to see if your username is in use visit this page first [http://folding.stanford.edu/download.html]("http://folding.stanford.edu/download.html"). There is a search box at the top that you can use to see if your selected username is in use.
[*]Have you team number ready, it is question two right after your username. You should use **45104** for this.
[*]If you have an old computer you should run deadlineness work units. To select the option to do this select yes when asked if you want to set advanced options, then continue to select the defaults until you are asked about deadlineless workunits and select yes.
[*]Finally here is a link to the original thread for using the finstall script from the folding community forums, it is where I found my answers and                      definitely the easiest way to get this working under Dapper Drake. [http://forum.folding-community.org/viewtopic.php?t=2283]("http://forum.folding-community.org/viewtopic.php?t=2283")[/LIST]Gook luck ~T313C0mun1s7

### Post by yaztromo on 2006-07-02
This is how I make mine start automatically at boot. It's taken from some howto posted eons ago.

sudo mkdir /home/fah
cd /home/fah
sudo wget [http://www.stanford.edu/group/pandegroup/release/FAH502-Linux.exe](http://www.stanford.edu/group/pandegroup/release/FAH502-Linux.exe)
sudo chmod +x FAH502-Linux.exe
sudo ./FAH502-Linux.exe

Enter the required info, and when F@H starts working on a work unit, close the client. Now to set up the startup scripts.

Make a file called fah in the /etc/init.d directory:
sudo gedit /etc/init.d/fah

Paste this in:
===========
#!/bin/sh
# /etc/init.d/fah for Ubuntu
# Start/stop/restart the F@H service.

fah_start() {
 if [ -x /home/fah/startfah.sh ]; then
   echo "Starting F@H:  /home/fah/startfah.sh"
   /home/fah/startfah.sh
 fi
}

fah_stop() {
 sudo killall FAH502-Linux.exe
}

fah_restart() {
 fah_stop
 sleep 2
 fah_start
}

case "$1" in
'start')
 fah_start
 ;;
'stop')
 fah_stop
 ;;
'restart')
 fah_restart
 ;;
*)
 fah_start
esac
===========

Save the file and close gedit, and finally make the file executable
sudo chmod +x /etc/init.d/fah

Now the startfah.sh script:
sudo gedit /home/fah/startfah.sh

And paste this into it:
==========
#!/bin/sh
cd /home/fah
/home/fah/FAH502-Linux.exe -forceasm -advmethods >/dev/null 2>&1 &
exit 0
==========

Make it executable:
sudo chmod +x /home/fah/startfah.sh

Make a symlink into the /etc/rc2.d directory:
ln -s /etc/init.d/fah /etc/rc2.d/S99fah

You can either test the script by rebooting or by typing the command:
sudo /etc/init.d/fah start

---

### Post by T313C0mun1s7 on 2006-07-02
**WOW!** That is a lot of work (read typing) just to get it to start automatically.

I just did exactly like I put into the code box on my prior post, and answered the questions asked. People are making this far too hard. Don't over think this, just run the finstall script and let it do its job.

Yes I have rebooted. Yes it restarted on its own, each instance has a nice value of 19, and both of my processors are running 100% all the time, yet I have no loss in responciveness and performance. The Windows version of the console client is actually more confusing to setup than the Linux version if you use the finstall script. In Windows rather than starting the service it starts in console mode until the first reboot, then to make matters worse (from the best I can tell) it no longer updates the log or unitinfo.txt files running as a Windows service. At least with the Linux Version I can see what is going on.

Initially I checked my progress like this:
```
cat foldingathome/CPU1/unitinfo.txt && cat foldingathome/CPU2/unitinfo.txt
``` 
but that was before I found the gDesklet gauges I posted about earlier.

**EDIT:** From the head of the script - these comments should clarify what it does, and on which operating systems. [B]Yes it generates init scripts, yes it works braindead easy on Ubuntu, Yes if you are using OS X you can use this same script.
[/B]```
FAH_Install_Version="4.8"
#
# This is FAH ("Folding At Home") client installation script.
# To get to know more about FAH go to http://folding.stanford.edu.
#
# To run this script You should download it and use command
# 'chmod +x finstall; ./finstall' or if the default shell is not
# Bash, use 'chmod +x finstall; bash -c "./finstall"'.
#
# It will try to download, place and configure seperate FAH clients
# (Fclient) for each CPU to $Fdir subdirectories.
# At the end it will generate an init/startup (*) script (./folding) for 
# Linux, FreeBSD, MacOSX, OpenBSD and possibly some other *nix compatible 
# OSes as well.
#
# (*) thanks go to Den for the backbone of this script.
#
# FAH client(s) will be run with the installing account's privileges. So
# when you run ./finstall as regular user then all files/directories
# are generated with this user's privileges and FAH services will be run
# as this user (not as root).
#
# If You want to run FAH client(s) under root privileges, then run this
# script as a 'root' user.
#
# Requirements: actually none but it is better to have wget/curl installed.
# Also this script uses some external utilities: "pidof"*, "kill", "awk", "ps",
# "ls", "cat", "grep", "tr"*, "cut", "md5sum"*, "wget"*, "wc", "tail", "more"
# "less", "curl"*, "tar" and "ed".
# I would like to get rid of dependency to these, but it may be very hard 
# to implement...
```

### Post by jpkotta on 2006-07-02
[https://wiki.ubuntu.com/FoldingAtHome](https://wiki.ubuntu.com/FoldingAtHome)

You can get to the wiki through the wiki link at the top of any forum page.  Once in the wiki, search for "folding".  I don't know how much easier it could be to find, but until you know it can be kind of non-obvious.  Bookmark it once you get there, because the wiki is full of useful information, and is usually clearer than the forums.

If you use the scripts there, then FAH will start at boot, and run on every processor you have.  I've never used finstall, but I hear that it's very good too.

### Post by drizek on 2006-07-11
40 is fine. You should only be worried about a temp like that if it means that it is burning your lap or doing something else that is harmfull. These cpus can handle running at 70C just fine, and anything around 50 is totally acceptable.

### Post by T313C0mun1s7 on 2006-07-12

There are two different methods to create the url. One simply uses the user id from folding.extreameoverclocking.com, the other has you specify user and team by name. The latter is what you are trying to do.[INDENT]From the sig images page:
**First** - You can use the UserID from the EOC Stats:
 - [http://folding.extremeoverclocking.com/sigs/sigimage.php?u=32359](http://folding.extremeoverclocking.com/sigs/sigimage.php?u=32359) 

**Second** - You can use your User Name + Team ID
 - [http://folding.extremeoverclocking.com/sigs/sigimage.php?un=HotRod&t=11314](http://folding.extremeoverclocking.com/sigs/sigimage.php?un=HotRod&t=11314) 
[/INDENT]After you have that down, then you can worry about extra options. I kinda like bg=2, but the information is not as easy to understand to those that don't understand short labels.
i.e. - [http://folding.extremeoverclocking.com/sigs/sigimage.php?u=188072&bg=2](http://folding.extremeoverclocking.com/sigs/sigimage.php?u=188072&bg=2)
[IMG]http://folding.extremeoverclocking.com/sigs/sigimage.php?u=188072&bg=2[/IMG]

### Post by T313C0mun1s7 on 2006-07-31
I just did this for another thread so I though I would cross post it here as it is relevant. Almost all of this information is already in this thread, but this puts it in one easy to read place. Also I have just complied info from elsewhere and I take no credit for anything that is here (except the hints at the end that is from a previous post of mine in this thread). Maybe we could add this to the FoldingAtHome page in the wiki? If so I would be willing to do that. I could also put together some stuff on Dynamic Sig graphics that are available and where. This forum doesn't allow graphics in the sig, but you can insert a image manually at the end of your post :lol:

> **Stew2 said:**
> Could you send me a link to a simple install script for the folding program? I tried it once before and messed up the install. I would be happy to contribute my spare CPU cycles! :D  Thanks


1. Download the finstall [http://www.vendomar.ee/~ivo/finstall]("http://www.vendomar.ee/%7Eivo/finstall") either with some browser and upload it to this box with sftp/ftp or if wget is available type:
```
wget -c http://www.vendomar.ee/~ivo/finstall
``` 
 2. Make the script runnable:
```
chmod +x finstall
``` 

3. Start it:
```
./finstall
```  
After the client is installed You can start/stop/... FAH client with ./foldingathome/folding script. For Example(s)

```

~/foldingathome/folding start

or

~/foldingathome/folding stop

or

~/foldingathome/folding status

``` 
For me this was all I needed as it automatically created the init scripts I needed to start after reboot. However the init scripts don't seem to work for everyone, so if you need to do it manually:

1.  Make a file called foldingathome in the /etc/init.d directory:
```
 sudo gedit /etc/init.d/foldingathome
``` 
2.  Paste this in:
```

#!/bin/sh
# /etc/init.d/foldingathome for Ubuntu
# Start the F@H service.

pushd /home/[COLOR=Red]YOUR_USERNAME_HERE[/COLOR]/foldingathome/
su [COLOR=Red]YOUR_USERNAME_HERE[/COLOR] -c "screen -d -m ./folding start"
popd

``` 
3. Save and exit

Here are a couple more hints to make things go smoother:[LIST=1]
[*]Pick a username before you start, to see if your username is in use visit this page first [http://folding.stanford.edu/download.html](http://folding.stanford.edu/download.html). There is a search box at the top that you can use to see if your selected username is in use.
[*]Have you team number ready, it is question two right after your username. You should use **45104** for this.
[*]If you have an old computer you should run deadlineness work units. To select the option to do this select yes when asked if you want to set advanced options, then continue to select the defaults until you are asked about deadlineless workunits and select yes.
[*]Finally here is a link to the original thread for using the finstall script from the folding community forums, it is where I found my answers and definitely the easiest way to get this working under Dapper Drake. [http://forum.folding-community.org/viewtopic.php?t=2283](http://forum.folding-community.org/viewtopic.php?t=2283)[/LIST][IMG]http://dcsig.liquidninjas.com/store/dcsig_3687_2096.png[/IMG][IMG]http://folding.extremeoverclocking.com/sigs/sigimage.php?u=188072[/IMG]

---

### Post by T313C0mun1s7 on 2006-08-02
> **rattlerviper said:**
> HELP!!!!

2. Paste this in:
Code:

#!/bin/sh # /etc/init.d/foldingathome for Ubuntu # Start the F@H service. pushd /home/YOUR_USERNAME_HERE/foldingathome/ su YOUR_USERNAME_HERE -c "screen -d -m ./folding start" popd


You don't have it all run together on one line like that do you? It should look more like this:
```

#!/bin/sh
# /etc/init.d/foldingathome for Ubuntu
# Start the F@H service.

pushd /home/[COLOR=Red]YOUR_USERNAME_HERE[/COLOR]/foldingathome/
su [COLOR=Red]YOUR_USERNAME_HERE[/COLOR] -c "screen -d -m ./folding start"
popd
``` 
That is how it is formatted on the wiki. 

Thanks for pointing out that it is not working however, I forgot to say that you need to make a symlink into the /etc/rc2.d directory:
```

sudo ln -s /etc/init.d/foldingathome /etc/rc2.d/S99fah
``` 

I will add that to the wiki right now. I think that will fix it. If not let me know.

### Post by jpkotta on 2006-08-03
Just installing an init script and an rc.d symlink won't start it.  You have to run the command to get it to start immediately.

```
sudo /etc/init.d/foldingathome start
```

---

### Post by jpkotta on 2006-08-03
> **fourchannel said:**
> Hi guys, I justed started. Daemon works wonderfully, starts at boot no probs. The fact that it's a ".exe" gets me everytime lol.

But I did some searching and tried to find the answer but I'm still gonna ask cause I want to be sure.

After F@H has been running for a little bit, the gnome sensors applets reports that my cpu temp is right around 55-56 Celcuis. I think this is ok. and I've got the shutdown temp set for 70 C. What do yall think?

and another thing.

I put the alarm command as "init 0" but I need root priviliges to shutdown and I don't know how to put that in there cause sudo needs you to type a password.

Here's a screenshot of what I'm talking about. Any input would be appreciated.

You could make the init command accessible to your user without authentication.

This brings up an editor for the sudoers file.  It is recommended that you use this command because it checks for errors in the sudoers file (I don't think I have to tell you that a bad sudoers file is Very Bad (but I guess I just did)).
```
sudo visudo
```

You can choose what ever editor you want (I think vi is hard):
```
export EDITOR=/usr/bin/emacs
```

Then add a line like this:
```

# I can run init without giving a password
jpkotta ALL = NOPASSWD: /sbin/init

```

---

### Post by jpkotta on 2006-10-12
You can see the progress by looking at /opt/foldingathome/1/FAHLog.txt.  There are various programs that will read this file and have a nice graphical display of your progress.  One is this: [http://sourceforge.net/project/showfiles.php?group_id=164311](http://sourceforge.net/project/showfiles.php?group_id=164311)

### Post by jpkotta on 2006-10-12
Sometimes the servers are overloaded.  All I can do is suggest that you leave it running for a couple days and see if it can connect then.  If it still doesn't, then you have a problem (but it still seems like you can connect to "assignment" server, so it's probably a server problem).

### Post by yorick on 2006-10-17
> **glotz said:**
> Will do. Thanks for the hand holding. Let's hope it fixes itself...

I had the same problem when I re-installed the client a week ago. It was because I chose to receive only work units without deadlines. It seems there is a shortage of these WU's. 

If you have a similar problem I would suggest configuring the client again and choosing to also receive WU's with deadlines.

HTH.

### Post by jpkotta on 2006-10-21
Yes, I've got it running on edgy.  People have been having a lot of problems with it though.  Just so we're on the same page, you're using the beta fah_install script from [https://help.ubuntu.com/community/FoldingAtHome](https://help.ubuntu.com/community/FoldingAtHome), correct?  If you do not update from that, you will have trouble.  Unpack the tar file into some directory, go to the fah_install directory that gets created, and run
```
sudo ./install.sh update
```

BTW, we are discussing Edgy problems in the HowTo thread: [http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=101817](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=101817)

---

### Post by jpkotta on 2006-12-19
> **D!mon said:**
> Just joined the team, user D!mon. I have several questions:
I'm running folding@home at work, thereby I use windows version (GUI version, the first link at the download page).

1. When I will restart my computer, will it start automatically and  continue from last time? Hope I wont have my data lost.

2. When I click on the tray icon, black display window is opened and redults of computing are painted into it. The question is: wouldn't this affect the performance? maybe it's better to use console version as a windows service or it doesnt matter?

In case you didn't get your questions answered elsewhere:

1. If you lose more than 15 minutes (the default interval for checkpoints) of work after rebooting then something went wrong.

2. You use some cycles displaying the graphics, but most are still used for folding.  I prefer the console version.  It is the fastest (but not by much) and it involves the least hassle once it's set up.

And we really do need more CPUs.  Look at how long it will take to get to the top 100: at least two years.

---

### Post by nanotube on 2007-02-07
hey all
i recently installed the fah client on my laptop, along with some nice cpulimiting.
i posted a pretty thorough howto about it on my ubuntu chronicles page here:
[http://pykeylogger.sourceforge.net/wiki/index.php/Ubuntu:Chronicles#Folding.40Home_.5BFAH.5D_on_a_Laptop](http://pykeylogger.sourceforge.net/wiki/index.php/Ubuntu:Chronicles#Folding.40Home_.5BFAH.5D_on_a_Laptop)
in case anyone is interested. :)

i have it running at 50% cpu load - that keeps the cpu nice and cool (fan keeps revving up if i just let it run at 100% idle load), so that should prevent any premature death due to folding. ;)

hope this comes in handy for some of you.

---

### Post by fourchannel on 2007-02-07
> i have it running at 50% cpu load - that keeps the cpu nice and cool (fan keeps revving up if i just let it run at 100% idle load), so that should prevent any premature death due to folding. :wink:I normally let my cpu fold at 100% for weeks of constant uptime, and it rests around low 50's celcius. I've had no problems with temp or unstability. You could probably let your cpu run at 100% and be ok, but the fans would always be churning. To put into perspective: AMD states that my processor can reach 85 C before being damaged, 30 degrees higher than what it normally stays at. Be sure to check your cpu's specs, but I would not consider folding to be an early death for the hardware   =D

---

### Post by glotz on 2007-02-07
I guess the issue with laptops usually is battery consumption.

---

### Post by nanotube on 2007-02-08
> **m.musashi said:**
> Thanks for the link. I hadn't seen that before. I did not install the way you suggested. Instead I dowloaded the linux 5.04 client from the website (which was actually a .exe - how does that work?). I followed the directions on the site and it seems to be working in a terminal. I'm pretty sure if I close it the program will stop. I guess that isn't a problem but maybe I should have read a bit more before jumping in.

i run it in the foreground in one of the vtys (ctl-alt-f2 :) ), with --verbosity=9 flag, so that i can monitor what it is doing. 

better than keeping an extra terminal window open on the desktop. and better than having it autostart with the system, because it's much easier to kill it if needed.

to start it in the "backgound", so that you can close the terminal window, just add a "&" to your commandline - that will background the process.

---

### Post by nanotube on 2007-02-08
> **fourchannel said:**
> I normally let my cpu fold at 100% for weeks of constant uptime, and it rests around low 50's celcius. I've had no problems with temp or unstability. You could probably let your cpu run at 100% and be ok, but the fans would always be churning. To put into perspective: AMD states that my processor can reach 85 C before being damaged, 30 degrees higher than what it normally stays at. Be sure to check your cpu's specs, but I would not consider folding to be an early death for the hardware   =D

well, it's not really about the death of the cpu, since the fan keeps my cpu cool, but more about the death of the fan, if it stays constantly on high (this is a laptop after all). 

another issue is the battery life - keeping the fan on high all the time eats it rather fast. though of course, most of the time it's running off the adapter anyway.

one more issue, probably the most important of all, is the noise. when the fan is on high, it's really loud, so i like to minimize that. mine is a dell 5150, maybe your laptop is quiet even with the fan on high, but not mine, unfortunately. :)

---

### Post by jpkotta on 2007-02-08
If you nice the client (I think to anything above zero), it will not kick up the CPU frequency.  Mine is niced at 19.  Then I have modified the power.sh script in /etc/acpi to turn the client on/off when the AC power is on/off.  See wiki for details.  

This cpulimit thing is pretty cool though.  If enough people want it, I'll add it to my scripts.

---

### Post by nanotube on 2007-02-08
> **jpkotta said:**
> If you nice the client (I think to anything above zero), it will not kick up the CPU frequency.  Mine is niced at 19.  Then I have modified the power.sh script in /etc/acpi to turn the client on/off when the AC power is on/off.  See wiki for details.  


oh, it doesn't make the cpu clock up, because the cores are niced to 19 by default. but even at half-speed (i've got a 3ghz, so my 'low' speed is 1.6ghz), running at 100% makes it warm up enough to kick up the fan into high gear. so basically, with the 50% limit, i have folding running at about a quarter of cpu capacity - first, it's clocked down to half, and then it's using half of its capacity. i have a 500k step WU, and it takes about 3.25 hours to finish 1% (5000steps). i suppose if i let the cpu clock up and max out, i theoretically could shave that down to less than an hour... but not gonna do that on a laptop. :)

the power.sh script mod sounds like a cool idea, i will check it out for my edification. :) but, which wiki do you refer to? could you please post a link? i looked around a bit, but couldn't find.

> 
This cpulimit thing is pretty cool though.  If enough people want it, I'll add it to my scripts.

it /is/ cool, ain't it? :) i'm thinking it will come in handy for other stuff too. when i was doing some lengthy computations in R, i had to put my laptop next to the window so that it doesn't keep heating up, now with cpulimit, i can just slap a limit on it and let it run.

---

better than keeping an extra terminal window open on the desktop. and better than having it autostart with the system, because it's much easier to kill it if needed.

to start it in the "backgound", so that you can close the terminal window, just add a "&" to your commandline - that will background the process.

Thanks.

ctl-alt-f2 gets you to a virtual terminal. you can log in there, then just 'cd' to the directory where you have FAH installed, and run it from there. then, just leave it alone and go back to the gui. To get back to the gui stuff, use ctl-alt-f7 (the x-windows stuff resides on vty7 by default). no need to "startx" again. 

by default, ubuntu has 6 vtys (f1 to f6, with the shortcuts), plus one for the gui, which is f7. 

hope that clears it up :)

### Post by nanotube on 2007-02-13
> **m.musashi said:**
> Okay, two questions for you - one on topic and one off. Off topic first. I know this isn't the right place but since it's realted to my running FAH I figue it's okay. Anyway, thinking my CPU was running a bit hot I bought some Antec silver (they didn't have artic) and tried to see if a better thermal grease would help. I think I used too much at first. However, my temps were pretty good. Running FAH I was sitting around 42c instead of the usualy 48c. However, I was worried that I had too much so I pulled the heatsink (almost wouldn't come off - a sign I did have too much?) and saw that while it wasn't running off the sides it was a bit much. There was still some oozing out the edge - a small lip of it on the heatsink. I cleaned it up and reapplied putting just a bit right in the middle like the artic silver web site suggested. I guess I should have read that first. However, now I'm running 47c with FAH. I think before I had a tad too much but now I might be a tad too little. I can keep messing with this but I figure I'm probably doing more harm than good. I think it's still better than the stock but wondering if I should do it again and go for near full coverage. Any expert advice?

well, if the difference was a full 5 degrees, then there's definitely room for improvement (though are you sure you ran it long enough to reach max temp, when you clocked the 42C measurement?). for reference purposes, here are some instructions straight from antec:
[http://www.antec.com/specs/instruction4.html](http://www.antec.com/specs/instruction4.html)
and here are some straight from arctic, are these the ones you used in your second time around?:
[http://www.arcticsilver.com/pdf/appinstruct/as5/ins_as5_amd_dual_wcap.pdf](http://www.arcticsilver.com/pdf/appinstruct/as5/ins_as5_amd_dual_wcap.pdf)

it certainly seems that you may have put too little thermal compound on in your second attempt. note that these thermal comps are non-conductive, so a little overrun doesn't make a big problem. you don't want too much grease, because the thermal conductivity is optimal when the grease layer is quite thin, but if you are going to err from the optimum, it is better to err slightly in the "more grease" direction than in the "less grease" direction. :)

so follow the antec instructions (clean stuff, then "prime" the heatsink with the compound), but in step 3 use a bit more grease than the "half a rice grain" that they recommend, use maybe 2 grains :). also, ignore step 4 and 5, and instead of spreading with blade, follow the arctic instructions for mounting - as in, leave the nice round mound of grease in the middle, lower the heatsink straight in, press it, and twist it back and forth just a tiny bit, then mount it.

well, that's my take on it. :) let me know how it turns out!

> 
Okay, back on topic. I decided to try your cpu limit how to but I didn't set up a start scrip. Instead I just ran
```
cpulimit -p `ps ax |grep -i fah |grep "RN+" |awk '{print $1}'` -l 50 &
```
in a terminal. It worked but I'm not sure how to stop it and let FAH run at 100% again. I suppose I could run the same thing with 100 at the end instead of 50 but I was wondering if I could just kill it. I didn't try that yet. Will ```
killall cpulimit
``` work? Also, when I ran it I did not use sudo as the FAH client is not a root process. However, it returned an error saying to run it as root. It still worked, however. Does it matter?

Thanks.

ok, to kill it, just do a killall cpulimit, you got it :) i don't know what will happen if you just run it again but with 100 - but i suspect that it will just stay at 50. so just kill the first one.

it runs "just fine" without root, but running it as root is better - it sets its own priority to -20, so that it can stay on top of whatever process it is limiting. not important for FAH though, since that is niced to the lowest priority of 19. so you really have no reason to run it as root. i just run it with sudo so it doesn't complain. :)

---

heh, well, basements are usually pretty cool even in the summer :). or you could try to get a better heatsink/fan combo, if it turns out that it runs too hot in the summer. also, the max rated temp for the 4800 seems to be 65C ([http://users.erols.com/chare/elec.htm)](http://users.erols.com/chare/elec.htm)), so as long as you stay at/under 50C or so, you should be fine.

> 
On another note, I just added my laptop to the mix. I have it running only 50% on one core because it seemed awful hot otherwise. yea, over 60C in pushing it. one thing i've found is that laptops' heatsink fins get clogged with dust over time, which really reduces the cooling efficiency. get it blown out (might have to take it apart partially to be able to get the duster tube to the heatsink), and then it will run much cooler. i end up having to do this on my dell 5150 a few times a year.

i as well have added another comp to the mix :) there's a desktop comp sitting in the office at school that is hardly ever used, but is left on most of the time. so i added a fah console client to start at system startup, so now that one should be crunching some FAH in my name :)

yea, i checked the rankings, and it appears that even in the low 100s, there are quite a few people with 0 activity in the last 50 days. so it seems that we may stand a good chance of even breaking into the top 100.

well, the thing with the 5150 is that it's a "power" system, so it's kinda heavy and bulky. but, that means they have a bit more room in there to slip in a better heatsink/fan combo than in your regular "slim and light" laptop. i think that's the key. 

but for your case, since lifting it up makes such a big difference, i'd suggest getting one of those laptop cooling pads (you know, the flat platform with a couple of fans in it. you can see a couple different ones here, e.g.: [http://www.compusa.com/products/products.asp?N=200486)](http://www.compusa.com/products/products.asp?N=200486)). those run under 20 bucks now, and reputedly can make a big difference in temperature.

well, i also tweaked the fan control so that it keeps the cpu cooler (check my customization howto in the sig). otherwise, by default, the fan wouldn't even turn on until the CPU hit like 55 or 60 (iirc). that's probably another thing you could try.

### Post by nanotube on 2007-02-18
> **m.musashi said:**
> I let mine run at 100% for about a day and half and finally finished the wu my laptop was running. However, I noticed something else. I would have thought the CPU running at 100% (even if just on one core) would scale up to it's max speed. My athlon on the desktop does this. But on the laptop, it stayed at 1000mhz the whole time. In fact, even if I run something like CPU burn, it still only sits at 1000mhz unless I run twice (one on each core). It seems pretty restrictive on when it scales. My wife's computer (also running edgy) scales if I just sneeze. It's an older pentium so that may have something to do with it. I suppose not scaling would save battery but when something like fah is running full tilt you would think that would meet the requirement - especially when not on battery. Do you think this is normal behavior for a core duo or a potential problem?

i think this has to do with the fact that the fah core runs at a very low priority (nice 19), and that's why it doesn't scale up. that is expected behavior. if you re-nice it to 0 (default for user processes), i bet you will see the cpu scaling up. give it a shot, and see what happens ('man nice' for a nice manual :)). 

> 
Congrats. It's great to get that first one and see your contribution. I see that you have two done now. Letting a desktop sit and run is probably the best way to do this. I have 5 WUs now and my 6th should finish today. I hope to break into the top 200 before the end of the week.

### Post by laredo7mm on 2007-02-19
> **m.musashi said:**
> Damn. That's fast. I have a athlon 4800 2.4ghz and it takes me 1.5 days to do a little 180 some point WU. How did you manage to do such a big point WU in so little time?

### Post by nanotube on 2007-02-20

ppd = points per day. with his speed and 1760pt WU, to calc pt per day we do:
> 23*100/60/24
[1] 1.597222
> 1760/1.597
[1] 1102.066

:)

### Post by laredo7mm on 2007-02-21
> **m.musashi said:**
> ... I tried to use the nice option but I don't see that it does anything. On my laptop I ran```
nice -n 1 ./fah-something.exe
``` but it still seemes to run at 1000mhz. I re-niced to -5 and there is no change. Of course I really don't know how to use the nice bit but I think I did it right...

You can check out your nice values, and change them, in the system monitor under the processes tab.  I usually still do it by command line in the terminal since that is the way I did it in SuSe before switching to Ubuntu.

In the terminal type in "ps aux"  That will list your processes and their PID.  then invoke your renice command:

"sudo renice -19 -p xxxxx"

Where xxxxx is the PID of the process you want to change the priority of.

---

In the terminal type in "ps aux"  That will list your processes and their PID.  then invoke your renice command:

"sudo renice -19 -p xxxxx"

Where xxxxx is the PID of the process you want to change the priority of.

### Post by nanotube on 2007-02-22
> **laredo7mm said:**
> Well, I ordered that second dual core system.  I couldn't resist. :)

well, i don't "know" about clustering, but this link ought to give you a good start:
[http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_cluster](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_cluster)

the thing is, i don't understand why you want to cluster these comps to run FAH. since fah is already a distributed computing project, all you would have to do to run fah on a "cluster" of 26+GHz of processing power is simply install a fah client on each of the machines! :) 

my understanding is that clustering is only useful for a certain subset of tasks that can be easily split into multiple processes (e.g. what fah does), so it's not like your desktop will suddenly be faster by having a cluster farm "attached" to it. :)

p.s. that new box you got looks like really nice bang/buck!

---

### Post by laredo7mm on 2007-02-22
> **nanotube said:**
> ...my understanding is that clustering is only useful for a certain subset of tasks that can be easily split into multiple processes (e.g. what fah does), so it's not like your desktop will suddenly be faster by having a cluster farm "attached" to it. :)

Yeah I found that out last night when I was doing some searching on Folding Farms.  A Folding Farm (from what I understand) is basically a bunch of computers each working on their own WU, not sharing the processing load.  That kind of took the wind out of my sales, that is just not a cool as having a mini supercomputer.

But it could still be done relatively cheaply since you could do a diskless farm and have each slave/client machine boot from the main server via the network.  That would save some $$$ in hard drives.  

Oh I can see it now, a bunch of raw mother boards and power supplies strewn around my house all connected with a web of Cat5. :)

### Post by laredo7mm on 2007-02-23
> **m.musashi said:**
> ...It's actually not cpu-limited. It's using 50% of a dual core or 100% of one core. No matter what though, it stays at 1000mhz...

Is yours a dual core?  I remember reading somewhere that if you are running a dual core with the non SMP core that you have to run two instances of FAH.  IIRC you would have to have two FAH directories and configure each with a different machine ID.  One FAH client would be configured with machine ID 1 and the other with machine ID 2.  Then when you start each FAH client from it respective directory use the "-local" flag so it writes it output only to the directory it is running from.

I can't remember where I read that, it might be from the FAH website.

OK, I found it on FAH's website but it applies to Windows: 

> **Does Folding@home run on dual processor or multi-core machines? Yes, you can in two ways. For linux or OSX/Intel, one can run our SMP client.**

For other platforms, additional processors must run the console version (with the "-local" command-line argument if run on Windows). First, make additional directories for each processor and copy the FAH Console executable file into each. Then configure them with the -config switch, filling in settings for each. It is very important to make sure that under the "Advanced Settings" option each copy is given a unique machine ID (from 1 to 8 ). The first copy will default to a machine ID of 1, so additional copies should be given IDs of 2, 3, 4, etc. Each may then be run out of their installed directory, using the -local switch on windows.


Are you running the SMP client on your laptop?

---

### Post by jpkotta on 2007-02-23
For renicing:

```
sudo renice 0 -u foldingathome
```

This assumes you used the fah_install script from the wiki ([https://help.ubuntu.com/community/FoldingAtHome)](https://help.ubuntu.com/community/FoldingAtHome)).  You must renice to 0 (or higher priority), otherwise the cpufreq governor doesn't kick up the frequency (at least it won't on my laptop).  The -u switch renices all processes owned by the specified user.  You can change the initial nice value permanently by editing the /etc/init.d/foldingathome script (look for --nicevalue).  Reinstall with the latest version to make it use all of your cores if it is only using one.

### Post by m.musashi on 2007-03-01
Anyone know what
```
SKB BUG: Invalid trusize (4072) len=16384, sizeof (sk_buff)=232
```
means? I have seen this a couple times using -verbosity 9 to run FAH. The WU that returned similar SKB BUG lines did finish so it doesn't seem to be a fatal error. Just wondering if it's something that can be fixed or just part of the normal FAH operation.

On another note. My 64bit via vmware has proved to be successful. I just got a big boost today thanks to a 1700 point WU that finished running on a 64bit server in vmware. If you have a dual core I suggest looking into this option. You don't have to reinstall your OS if you are using 32bit but can benefit from the 64bit SMP client that gives better points. Running in vmware I can finish a 1700 point job in about the same time it takes to finish a 180 point job on a non-smp client. That's a big payoff. Granted I'm having some wierd clock issues but it doesn't seem to affect the WU so I guess it's nothing to worry about.

---

### Post by TLE on 2007-03-02
Does anyone know how I can scale the cpu-usage to something like 90% by just editing the cfg file. I rather do it that way so I'm certain I wont change anything else. Currently myclient.cfg looks like this:
```
[settings]
username=TLE
team=45104
asknet=no
machineid=1
local=9
bigpackets=yes

[http]
active=no
host=localhost
port=8080

[core]
priority=0
checkpoint=3
```

---

### Post by nanotube on 2007-03-02
> **TLE said:**
> Does anyone know how I can scale the cpu-usage to something like 90% by just editing the cfg file. I rather do it that way so I'm certain I wont change anything else. 

afaik, the linux client does not have built in cpu throttling. to throttle cpu, you gotta use an external utility, called cpulimit. check my customization howto (link in sig) in the f@h section for how to set that up...

### Post by nanotube on 2007-03-08
> **m.musashi said:**
> So like SAS? That is what I use for my program but it's only on Windows afaik. I guess I'll have to check it out.

yea, i guess you could say it's like sas. only it's better :) heh, well, it's better in some respects, namely, it is much more programmable, and has a lot of up-to-date statistical techniques available in the packages, and it is a real full-fledged programming language. on the other hand, SAS may do some "standard" things with slightly less code and gives more output by default. 

so yea, check R out. if you've ever done any coding, you would find in more intuitive than SAS syntax.

### Post by T313C0mun1s7 on 2007-03-17
The smaller ones can be just as quality and have just as much cooling as the full size AT power supplies. The only difference is form factor. AT motherboards were large and required a lot of space, so the cases were made to fit. When ATX came around they didn't really change the size of the power supply for backward compatibility reasons. As the demand for more space saving designs came about, and as ATX was approaching a second version of the standard, a smaller standard profile came around. PSUs are normally rated by wattage, but this is misleading. There are six power buses in a PSU, +3.3v +5v +12v -12v -5v and -5vSB. The power rating is the total power of all buses. Modern  ATX mother boards use the +12v bus almost exclusively, and Pentuim III and older used the +5v. Many cheap PSU have a high amperage ratting on the never used buses to boost their power rating knowing they will not get used. Also, since ATX really only uses those two power buses, smaller PSUs cut power to the others to reduce heat. Look for one that has at least a 15A rating for the +5v and a 30A rating on the +12v and you will have more than enough power for what ever you do. I can not attest to the quality of this one as I have not used it, but I give it of an example of one with sufficient power available on the buses you need it for, and good cooling. [_Example_]("http://www.mdofpc.com/onlinestore/diablotek-apower-420watt-microatx-dual-60mm-fans-sataready-power-supply-p-911612.html") and if you want to spend some money [Another Example]("http://www.mdofpc.com/onlinestore/apevia-beast-power-680watt-atx-triple-fan-aluminum-sliready-sata-ready-power-supply-p-917393.html?download_software=no")

A case is really designed to mount one or the other. If you want to go modifying your case just to make yourself feel like you have a better PSU, go ahead. Just be prepared to get a tattoo that says "naive" on your forehead if you tell any good computer tech what you have done.

Not to be overly judgmental, but if your local computer store does not have these, it is not much of a computer store. They are used in almost all low profile and small form factor applications. This is true both of name brand and build your own applications. Just look at the cube shape Shuttle cases (or any micro ATX case) as well as the small form factor computers made by Acer, Compaq, Dell, eMachine, Gateway, HP, and others. All of them use these power supplies. If you have ever cracked open a power supply (and you shouldn't) you would notice how much empty space there is in there. Size does not make quality. Quality components and good heat dissipation make quality.

---

### Post by T313C0mun1s7 on 2007-03-18
Actually the rating is not good at all. You might notice from my prior post that I stated you need 30 Amps on the +12v bus. Your PSU only had 14 Amps. Not even half, you were woefully under rated.

In fact it is very hard if not impossible to find a case with a bundled in PSU where the PSU is going to cut it. This is why "White Box" PCs that just use the case with the bundled PSU and build from that are seldom as stable as brand name PCs. In brand name PCs the PSU is specified by the engineers to be sufficient to the components installed. You can get "White Box" PCs of quality, but you have to really look. For some reason people will pay for quality in every other component, but over look the thing that powers the entire unit. The typical problems seen by a under rated PSU is lockups, failure to boot, and spontaneous reboots.

T313C0mun1s7 is a blending of Telecom and Communist. It has nothing to do with my political views, but I do agree that most people misunderstand that socialism  is not communism. If you look I don't think Marx actually intended anything as far as forming a government. He recognized that human nature and the Utopian view he created in the Communist Manifesto were mutually exclusive and stated that it could never really exist. He was half right, it can never exist with out divine intervention, and since many if not most communists are Atheist man will never bring about communism that works - only God can do that. What my handle refers to is the spirit of sharing and free information exchange that existed in the 60s and 70s computer and telecommunications movement, and still exists today through the culture of open source and the like. It is this spirit that drew me into IT back when I was eight. I have been a member of one informational exchange or another ever since. [URL="http://www.google.com/search?q=T313C0mun1s7"]SEE GOOGLE SEARCH
[/URL]

### Post by m.musashi on 2007-03-20
FAH released their SMP client for windoes so Linux users no longer have that edge. However, the good news is that if you have a dual core CPU that is not 64 bit (and therefore can't run the Linux SMP client) you can now run it in windows and enjoy the benefits of SMP and you don't have to tell anyone you are using windows. I have a core duo laptop that won't run the 64 bit Linux SMP (core duo is 32 bit and core 2 duo is 64). However, it is now folding for team ubuntu. I hope that's okay:). You could probably do this via wine, vmware or virtualbox as well if you didn't want to install windows, but I haven't tried so that's not a recommendation.

### Post by laredo7mm on 2007-04-19
Bad news for all Linux SMP folders:

F@H has come out with two new WU's, 2608 and 2609.  2608 is worth 1385 points and 2609 is worth 1523 points.  These two WU's are much more resource dependent and rely heavily on the amount of L2 cache your processor has.

On my AMD X2's with 512Mb of L2 cache, these WU's are only netting about 700 ppd, compared to 1050 ppd when running a 2604 or 2605 WU.  I am experiencing a 30% drop in ppd and others are reporting a 50% decrease in ppd.

The two new WU's were benchmarked on F@H's computer which runs a quad-core Woodcrest processor with 4Mb of L2 Cache on each core.  It is the same computer that they used to benchmark the other SMP WU's, but the new ones are more cache dependent.

I am running two of these WU's right now, and they are going to hurt. :sad:  I hope I don't keep getting too many more of these.

### Post by laredo7mm on 2007-04-21
> **spamzilla said:**
> ...I'm not sure if it's running and how (or if) I can configure it at all.

The Linux client runs in a terminal.  I run mine on tty1 since I usually stop gdm when I am not using it.  Check out glotz's link in his sig for more details, and you can also check out F@H web site's FAQ.

But basically in a command line type in the following (while in your folding directory):

```
./fah5
```

Or whatever the executable file name is.  fah5 is the SMP client, the other clients have a different name.  The first time you run the program it will go through the configuration.  After that if you want to change your settings type in the following:

```
./fah5 -configonly
```

That will rerun the configuration but not run the client.

If you want to rerun the configuration and then have the client start, enter this:

```
./fah5 -config
```

To run the client and have it output as much info as possible to the log file, run this command:

```
./fah5 -verbosity 9
```


I hope that helps, let us know if you have any more problems.

### Post by laredo7mm on 2007-04-24
TLE, looks like the servers that FAH is trying to connect to for that WU are not working correctly.

171.65.103.68 is reported to be "rejecting" which means it is supposed to be working but it isn't.

171.65.103.100 says it is not serving WU's and "Not Accept" means that the server is at standby and they don't expect it to be  accepting connections (and it isn't).

You should still be able to fold and return different WU's while the finished one is held in que.  You might ultimately end up loosing that finished WU if  the servers don't come back on line.

### Post by ruudiculus on 2007-04-29
Poor dog! ;)

When I run it on my AMD32 2.2GHz PC (Zahlman fan at full throttle), ambient temperature of 20 degrees Celsius the CPU temperature reaches 50 easily. Your CPU's overheating circuit will kick in when the CPU core reaches a temperature around 80 degrees. If you think your ambient temperature will be higher than 50 degrees C, then I think your PC might go into a reset (since it is reaching the 80 degrees limit). I don't know if your BIOS can be set to "shutdown" instead of "reset" in such a situation, because then you can test it safely while leaving home. Otherwise it will reset again and again until you come home; I wouldn't advice that!

---

One of my two cores reach 50 degrees (ambient temps never get more than 80 degrees Fahrenheit, and are usually 10 degrees Fahrenheit lower when I'm home). What's interesting is that there is sometimes as much as a 5 degree difference in the temps on both my cores.

I'm starting to think that this SMP beta client isn't worth running... my PPH is currently 15.737, but I was expecting to get something much higher on an Athlon X2 5200+. I haven't tried the regular client on this system yet, but I'll probably give it a try after this current work unit gets uploaded (which will hopefully be by Monday).

What is a normal PPH for an Athlon X2 5200+?

50 degrees is O.K., from what I have read.  The X2 5200+ is a dual core with 1Gb cache, right?  You should be getting more than 16 pph.  On my three AMD dual cores running between 2.2 to 2.4 Ghz, I get from 700 to 1100 ppd depending on which work unit I am running.  The 2604's and 2605's are the best for me.  The 2608/9's kill my ppd because they need more L2 cache, and my procs only have 512Mb.

A 2604/5 will take about 24 minutes per 1% and the 2608/9's take about 30 minutes per 1%.  The 2604/5's are worth 1760 points and the 2608/9's are 1385 and 1532.

If your proc is single core, I don't think you want to run the SMP client.  The SMP client was originally intended for quad core procs, but it does run O.K. on dual cores.

### Post by NacIK on 2007-05-11
I am running Feisty and have a Dual-Core Opteron.  Can anyone help me get my computer folding.  I have been trying for a week but can't seem to get the program installed.  Maby it is because I am running the AMD64 version of Ubuntu.

---

### Post by D!mon on 2007-05-11
> **NacIK said:**
> I am running Feisty and have a Dual-Core Opteron.  Can anyone help me get my computer folding.  I have been trying for a week but can't seem to get the program installed.  Maby it is because I am running the AMD64 version of Ubuntu.

Use this guide: [http://www.rage3d.com/board/showthread.php?t=33880616](http://www.rage3d.com/board/showthread.php?t=33880616)
Don't forget to set  	 45104 team number!!!

> 
5 = Download & Configure SMP Folding @ Home for Linux
Now we need to download and configure the linux SMP client.
Open a new terminal session. Now we need to create the working directory, download the client and configure it with your username and team number (45104!!!!). Type:
Code:

mkdir -p ~/FAH
cd ~/FAH
wget [http://folding.stanford.edu/release/FAH_SMP_Linux.tgz](http://folding.stanford.edu/release/FAH_SMP_Linux.tgz)
tar xzf FAH_SMP_Linux.tgz
./fah5 -configonly

note the ~/ is a shortcut for /home/userid. [thanks MDC!]

5a = Configure F@H autostart with ubuntu
Now all that remains is to get this sucker up and folding! It would be nice to start it automatically when the OS starts, so now in terminal we do the following:
Code:

sudo nano /etc/rc.local

This opens the rc.local file for editing. Above the line that reads 'exit 0' (last line), add the following entry:
Code:

sudo sh -c "cd /home/user/FAH; ./fah5 -local -forceasm -verbosity 9"

note:
- change 'user/FAH'to your profile name and folding install directory - use the pwd command to find your full path.
- the example above uses the -local and verbosity 9 flags. remove them if you don't want to run them, but they're a good idea.
- the example also uses the -forceasm flag - the beta client is having problems inappropriately disabling SSE. use this to force it on for full performance.
Press Ctrl-O and hit enter to save your changes, then Ctrl-X to exit.
Close terminal.
Reboot and everything should come up automagically! Login and to monitor your event log, with autorefresh every60 seconds, open terminal and type:
Code:

cd ~/FAH
tail -s 60 -f FAHlog.txt




---

### Post by laredo7mm on 2007-05-11
> **D!mon said:**
> ...Don't remember to set 45104 team number!!!

No! Don't **forget** to set 45104 as the team number.  :):)

Also make sure you install the **ia32-libs** **package** from the repositories.  The SMP client needs that when running on 64bit Ubuntu.  The SMP client is 32bit, but the core that does the calculations is 64bit, so the **ia32-libs package** is needed.

So just do a search for ia32-libs in Synaptic and check the box to install (there will be a few dependencies that come up, install those too).

Or in a terminal do:

```
sudo apt-get install ia32-libs
```

### Post by Pugwash on 2007-05-14
Hi, I've recently upgraded to feisty and f@h seems to send my cpu (core2duo t5500, on a dell 6400 laptop) into its  maximum frequency (1.66ghz), dapper ran f@h at 1 ghz. I've  tried doing the following, but it seems to have no effect:

```
 sudo -i
echo 1 > /sys/devices/system/cpu/cpu0/cpufreq/ondemand/ignore_nice_load 
```

As mentioned here - [https://help.ubuntu.com/community/FoldingAtHome](https://help.ubuntu.com/community/FoldingAtHome)

### Post by Enverex on 2007-05-14
> **Swab said:**
> It won't effect your Windows gaming as the client program only uses spare clock cycles.

This isn't true, it doesn't affect ALL games, but it does adversely affect some. I remember (I was part of a big folding team) that it would slow down both GTA3 and Max Payne 2 quite considerably (but not the other games I was playing at the time). So it's something to keep an eye on.

Something else to remember if no-ones mentioned it already. If you run this on a laptop you'll max out the processor so you'll have it running at its hottest and most likely cause the fans to run at max the entire time, it will also cripple battery life unless you disable it on battery.

---

### Post by m.musashi on 2007-05-14
> **Pugwash said:**
> Hi, I've recently upgraded to feisty and f@h seems to send my cpu (core2duo t5500, on a dell 6400 laptop) into its  maximum frequency (1.66ghz), dapper ran f@h at 1 ghz. I've  tried doing the following, but it seems to have no effect:

```
 sudo -i
echo 1 > /sys/devices/system/cpu/cpu0/cpufreq/ondemand/ignore_nice_load 
```

As mentioned here - [https://help.ubuntu.com/community/FoldingAtHome](https://help.ubuntu.com/community/FoldingAtHome)

Anyone know how to solve this?

Cheers

FAH is designed to run your CPU at 100%. As a result, that will also ramp up your clock speed. You can prevent this if you want but it's a couple of extra steps. Check out [this post](http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=2148154&postcount=600) or [this link](http://pykeylogger.sourceforge.net/wiki/index.php/Ubuntu:Chronicles#Folding.40Home_.5BFAH.5D_on_a_Laptop) for more info.

However, that may not actually keep your clock speed from ramping up. Even at 50% usage it might scale up. You can also install a tool to manually set frequencies (on a laptop - I've never used it on a desktop so I don't know if it works). Unfortunately, I can't remember how. The key words to search are probably "frequency" and "governor". Maybe someone else can fill in the missing link (no pun intended).

EDIT: Okay, I found [this link](http://ubuntuguide.org/wiki/Ubuntu_Edgy#How_to_enable_your_CPU.27s_Power_Saving.2FFrequency_Scaling_features). It might get you started.

---

### Post by aristotlewilde on 2007-05-20
I have been running the Windows client for a week or so (joined the DL.tv team after they mentioned it on the show).  

I tried setting it up on my Ubuntu Feisty Box, but I was getting two issues:
1) My (wired) internet connection kept quitting on me at random times
2) My CPU usage was stuck at 100% while FAH was running.

If someone could help me clear these two issues up, I'd gladly run the Linux client for the Ubuntu team (This machine has an AMD 3500+ w/ a gig of RAM.  I am sure it can contribute)

---

### Post by 5thfreedom on 2007-05-20
> **aristotlewilde said:**
> 
1) My (wired) internet connection kept quitting on me at random times
2) My CPU usage was stuck at 100% while FAH was running.


It is normal for the FAH client to use 100% of your spare cpu cycles. This will not affect the performance of your machine because it runs with idle priority and only uses as much of your cpu that isn't being used by other programs. I run it 24/7 and while I play games, burn dvds, and watch movies with absolutely no performance hit. The only problem that some people have with the processor humming along at 100% all the time is keeping their computer cool. So keep an eye on your temps when you run the client.

As for your internet connection problem, I don't see how that could be related to FAH. Do you not have the connection problem when you aren't running the client?

BTW, a few of us fold for TeamUbuntu even on our Windows machines. Hope to see you join the team!

---

### Post by Enverex on 2007-05-20
> **5thfreedom said:**
> It is normal for the FAH client to use 100% of your spare cpu cycles. This will not affect the performance of your machine because it runs with idle priority and only uses as much of your cpu that isn't being used by other programs. I run it 24/7 and while I play games, burn dvds, and watch movies with absolutely no performance hit. 

Quoting myself from earlier. Replace "games" with "programs".

> **Enverex said:**
> This isn't true, it doesn't affect ALL games, but it does adversely affect some. I remember (I was part of a big folding team) that it would slow down both GTA3 and Max Payne 2 quite considerably (but not the other games I was playing at the time). So it's something to keep an eye on.

---

### Post by 5thfreedom on 2007-05-20
Thank you for expanding on my point Enverex. I suppose different people will have different experiences dependent on the programs that they use. This thread has gotten so huge that it's easy to miss things that people have said in the pages prior. It would be nice to have a forum dedicated to folding so people can get answers to their questions more effectively. 

Here is a good [[COLOR="Blue"]article[/COLOR]]("http://techreport.com/etc/2002q4/foldingimpact/index.x?pg=1") from The Tech Report on the performance impact of running FAH while using other programs. A little old, but still a good article.

---
