### Post by Spartan.II.117 on 2007-06-18
I'm finaiy back up and folding at full power(which isn't much...) so i'm leaving my computer on for the next week straight while i'm at camp. does anyone have any suggestions for optimising the speed that they can give me in the next four hours?

---

### Post by nanotube on 2007-06-18
> **Spartan.II.117 said:**
> I'm finaiy back up and folding at full power(which isn't much...) so i'm leaving my computer on for the next week straight while i'm at camp. does anyone have any suggestions for optimising the speed that they can give me in the next four hours?

hmm, well, if it's folding at 100% cpu, then that's basically all you're gonna get :)
just make sure to turn off any screensavers or other cpu-intensive processes you may have running, so that there is as little competition as possible for the cpu resources.

you might consider even running in console-mode only, to get rid of xorg and other hungry gui processes, even.

### Post by jpkotta on 2007-07-02
> **D!mon said:**
> Btw, there is new SMP beta - 5.91beta4; it says that previous expired on July 1st. It's interesting what changed and will it work better or maybe faster now :)

Yeah, I just noticed that.  I doubt that it will be any faster; it probably just has some bug fixes.  The client just downloads the cores; they are the things that actually do the simulation.  The client can download a new core any time it gets a new WU, so you will get new cores automatically when they are available.

### Post by Spartan.II.117 on 2007-08-13
Brenny: first, on linux folding at home runs in the backround, so it wont show up on any of your desktops. What kernel are you using? if your using the smp kernel you should be able to run two smp clients, which will take full advantage of your system but i'm not sure how well the smp kernel works with multiple processors. if you are using the generic kernel the best use would be two standard clients. this link has the install methods you need: [https://help.ubuntu.com/community/FoldingAtHome](https://help.ubuntu.com/community/FoldingAtHome)

### Post by Spartan.II.117 on 2007-08-14
you will lose the data from your curent wu, so let that finish, there is a command taat will make it stop after current wu, you might want to add that to your script for the time being, as far as a monitoring program,just something that will send you data directly, i gave a g15 keyboard so i sent my stats to that through proclcd and a script i found. (which i've made some significant modifications to so let me know if it would be useful and i'll send it to you. if you have any type of lcd screen, i'd recomend this) or search google for a linux folding at home monitor.

### Post by jpkotta on 2007-08-15
brennydoogles, if you want the most out of your computer, you need to get the SMP client.  It will only work on 64-bit systems (that is, kernel and userspace are 64-bit, not just hardware).  It does more work than running one client for each core.  If you don't want to go 64-bit, then just do what others have said and install a script from the wiki.

The following command will tell you pretty much everything Linux knows about your processor.
```
cat /proc/cpuinfo
```

---

### Post by Spartan.II.117 on 2007-08-16
well i went with 64bit ubuntu, so now i need to figure out how to get my perl script to run...(any suggestions?)
Here's the script:
[SIZE=1] #!/usr/bin/perl
use IO::Socket;
use Fcntl;





$LCDHOST = "172.0.0.1";
$LCDPORT = "13666";
$UNITINFO = "/opt/foldingathome/1/unitinfo.txt";
$CYCLE = 10;
$NAME = "Desktop";

sub lcd {
    ($data) = @_;
    print $lcdproc $data."\n";
    $res = <$lcdproc>;
}

sub updatescreen {

    if ($oldline1 ne $line1) {
        $oldline1=$line1;
        lcd("widget_set fathlcd line1 1 2 {$line1}");
    };
    if ($oldline2 ne $line2) {
        $oldline2=$line2;
        lcd("widget_set fathlcd line2 1 3 {$line2}");
    };
    if ($oldline3 ne $line3) {
        $oldline3=$line3;
        lcd("widget_set fathlcd line3 1 4 {$line3}");
    };
    if ($oldhbar ne $hbar) {
        $oldhbar=$hbar;
        lcd("widget_set fathlcd hbar 6 3 $hbar");
    };

};

sub calc{

 $percentage = `cat $UNITINFO | tail -n 1 | sed -e s/Progress..//`;
 chomp($percentage);
 $percentage =~ s/(\d+)\%.+/\1/;

 $name = `cat $UNITINFO | tail -n 4 | head -n 1 | sed -e s/Name..//`;
 chomp($name);

 $start = `cat $UNITINFO | tail -n 3 | head -n 1 | sed -e s/Download.time..//`;
 chomp($start);
 $start = `date -d "$start" +%s`;
 chomp($start);

if ($percentage == 0 ){
  $pterper = 0;
} else {
  $tperper = (time() - $start) / $percentage; 
}
 $seconds = (100 - $percentage)*$tperper;

 $hours = int($seconds / 3600);

 if ($hours > 23) {

  $days = int($seconds / 86400);
  $seconds -= 86400 * $days;
  $hours = int($seconds / 3600);
  $seconds -= 3600 * $hours;

  $tr = sprintf("%d d %d h",$days, $hours);

 } else {

  $hours = int($seconds / 3600);
  $seconds -= 3600 * $hours;

  $tr = sprintf("%d h",$hours);
 }

 $tremaining = "tRem ".$tr;

 $seconds = $percentage * $tperper;

 $hours = int($seconds / 3600);

 if ($hours>23) {

  $days = int($seconds / 86400);
  $seconds -= 86400 * $days;
  $hours = int($seconds / 3600);
  $seconds -= 3600 * $hours;

  $tr = sprintf("%d d %d h",$days, $hours);

 } else {

  $hours = int($seconds / 3600);
  $seconds -= 3600 * $hours;

  $tr = sprintf("%d h",$hours);
 }

 $trunning = "tRun ".$tr;

 return ($name,$tremaining,$trunning,$percentage);
}

$lcdproc = IO::Socket::INET->new(
        Proto     => "tcp",
        PeerAddr  => $LCDHOST,
        PeerPort  => $LCDPORT,
    ) || die "Cannot connect to LCDproc port on $LCDHOST:$LCDPORT\n";

$lcdproc->autoflush(1);

sleep 1;

print $lcdproc "hello\n";
@lcd_specs = split(/ /,<$lcdproc>);

$screen{wid} = $lcd_specs[7];
$screen{hgt} = $lcd_specs[9];
$screen{cellwid} = $lcd_specs[11];
$screen{cellhgt} = $lcd_specs[13];

$screen{pixwid} = $screen{wid}*$screen{cellwid};
$screen{pixhgt} = $screen{hgt}*$screen{cellhgt};

fcntl($lcdproc, F_SETFL, O_NONBLOCK);

lcd("client_set name {$NAME}");
lcd("screen_add fathlcd");
lcd("screen_set fathlcd name {$NAME}");

# if you like heartbeat , comment this line out
lcd("screen_set fathlcd heartbeat off");

lcd("widget_add fathlcd title title");
lcd("widget_set fathlcd title {$NAME}");

lcd("widget_add fathlcd line1 string");
lcd("widget_add fathlcd line2 string");
lcd("widget_add fathlcd line3 string");
lcd("widget_add fathlcd hbar hbar");

$line1 = "   [initializing]   ";
$line2 = " fathlcd 0.1   BETA ";
$line3 = "          buZz 2005 ";

$oldline1 = "";
$oldline2 = "";
$oldline3 = "";
$oldhbar = "";
$hbar = "";

updatescreen;
$count=0;

while(1)
{
    $ignore=0;

    while(defined($input = <$lcdproc>)) {

        @lines = split(/\n/, $input);
        foreach $line (@lines)
        {
        if ( $line =~ /^success$/ ) { next; } 
        if ( $line =~ /^ignore (\S)/ ) { $ignore = -1; } 
        }

    }

    if (!$ignore) {
        updatescreen;
    }

    sleep 1;

    ($name,$tr,$trun,$percentage) = &calc;

    $line1 = "$name";
    $line2 = $percentage."% [..........]";
    $hbar = $percentage;

    if ($count<($CYCLE*2)) {
        $line3 = $trun;
    } 
    if ($count<$CYCLE) {
        $line3 = $tr;
    } 
    if ($count==($CYCLE*2)) {
        $count=0;
        $line3 = $tr;
    }

    $count++;
}

close ($lcdproc) || die "close: $!";
exit;[/SIZE]

---

### Post by laredo7mm on 2007-08-21
> **Spartan.II.117 said:**
> Laredo how would i go about doing that?

It is not too bad, well I don't think it would be, I have never done it.  I don't use an install script or anything, I just download the tgz file from F@H, unpack it into a directory, and then open a terminal, cd to the directory where the client is located, and manually start the client by typing:

```

chmod +x FaH
./fah5
```You only need to do the chmod command the first time to make sure it is executable.

Now if you want to run two instances, you will need two directories, lets say folding1 and folding2, both with an unpacked fah tgz in them.  Do your chmod command to each, then do:

```
./fah5 -local -configonly
```To each client in each directory (or folder).  That will open the configuration for the client.  Go through all the normal info entry and where it asks you for machine ID, make one machine #1 and the other machine #2.

Now open a terminal, cd to one of your folding directories, and type in:

```
./fah5 -local -verbosity 9
```That will run that client and contain it to that specific folder and generate detailed log files.

Open another terminal and do the same for the second folding directory.

Now you should have two instances running.

Instead of running in a terminal, I typically do a control +alt +f1 to open a new tty and run fah from there.

I hope that makes sense, if not, let me know and I can try to explain it better.

---

A team of Ubuntu users may be able to make a bigger dent in this one. Also the individual that finds the best model is cited and given credit for finding the best lowest energy structure see [http://boinc.bakerlab.org/rosetta/rah_top_predictions.php]("http://boinc.bakerlab.org/rosetta/rah_top_predictions.php").

### Post by xzero1 on 2007-08-27
> i would say that we're doing the same thing with folding at home, and since the research will be publisher=d publicly there is no reason to spend time on the rosetta program rather than the folding at home one.

Let me try to make my case. As I understand it, folding at home uses a deterministic algorythms to build their proteins. It is slow and needs a tremendous amount of cpu time to fold for so many microseconds of folding. Rosetta uses a different approach: It is known that a correct fold has the lowest system energy level and Rosetta tries to find this low energy state. The problem is the search space is huge, so Rosetta tries a relatively inaccurate but very very fast fold and each run starts the fold differently. Now if the initial folds are chosen correctly, we can get very close to the actual final protein state or structure. The complete folding is done on a single computer, results are sent back and the lowest energy fold from all the runs is selected. Currently, the exact structure cannot be predicted using this method due, the author thinks, to not enough computers.

Project head scientist quote:
> It is clear for the still large number of proteins for which we are failing that the problem is not enough sampling, even with 100,000 independent folding runs we are not coming close enough to the native structure to land in its energy minimum. So we need more CPU power! it is kind of amazing that solving such a long standing scientific problem depends so crucially on the efforts of volunteers like yourselves!

Rosetta currently only has about 57 teraflops of power compared to about a  petaflop for folding at home. There is probably a minimum threshold of power needed to accurately predict the protein structures. Rosetta runs under BOINC (comming to folding at home) and so in time we will be able to allocate our computer power between both projects as we see fit. BTW, I am currently running a beta BOINC 64-bit under Feisty Fawn.

Wiki comparison of protein folding projects:
[http://boinc-wiki.ath.cx/What_Is_The_Difference_Between_The_Different_Protein_Projects%3B_Including_Folding%40Home%2C_Predictor%40Home%2C_Rosetta%40Home%2C_SIMAP%2C_and_World_Community_Grid%3F]("http://boinc-wiki.ath.cx/What_Is_The_Difference_Between_The_Different_Protein_Projects%3B_Including_Folding%40Home%2C_Predictor%40Home%2C_Rosetta%40Home%2C_SIMAP%2C_and_World_Community_Grid%3F")

I invite you to investigate the Rosetta project and consider my case.
[http://boinc.bakerlab.org/rosetta/]("http://boinc.bakerlab.org/rosetta/")

---

### Post by jpkotta on 2007-10-08
I've updated my fah_install script.  Get it in the wiki ([https://help.ubuntu.com/community/FoldingAtHome](https://help.ubuntu.com/community/FoldingAtHome)).  It adds the 6.00(beta1) client.  You should be able to update everything by running the following commands:

```
sudo /etc/init.d/foldingathome stop
sudo tar zcvf fahbck.tar.gz /opt/foldingathome 
sudo ./install.sh install
sudo /etc/init.d/foldingathome start
```

You will want to make sure you allow the installer to update the /etc/default/foldingathome file, since the 6.00(beta1) client needs an extra option for SMP work units.

---

### Post by ozzyprv on 2007-12-16

---

### Post by jpkotta on 2007-12-18
> **ozzyprv said:**
> I starting reading this post to find the answer to my question, but I gave up on page 20...

I installed folding at home about 12 hours ago. I used the script folding-0.5.2.1.
Is there any way to temporarily stop the program from running (my HD is REALLY noisy) and then restart it?

Thank you.

You may be running out of RAM.  If you run ```
free
``` and both "free" and "cached" are relatively small, and "swap" is relatively large, you are swapping heavily.

I believe there is an init script that folding.sh installs.

```
sudo /etc/init.d/folding stop
```

### Post by Jhongy on 2007-12-22
Fixed it...

It crashed reliably after about 10 mins or so of running it. Originally assumed it was CPU overheating -- but lm-sensors showed the temperature peaking after a few minutes, then not rising further (falling slightly).

Works like a charm now :-)

### Post by Red Shift on 2008-01-02
> **arashiko28 said:**
> OK, I want to join in, but despite I use Linux 24-7, I'm not a computer guru. I'm a med student. So... could someone please give a crash course for dummies to install and run this? please?

F@H does not have to be run on Wine.

The following is what I did to run the F@H client on a 32-bit operating system.

1.  Create a folder in your user account called Folding32.
2.  Download the 5.04 client from Stanford's site to the Folding32 folder. [http://folding.stanford.edu/English/Download](http://folding.stanford.edu/English/Download)
3.  Extract the tarball within the Folding32 folder.  Right-click > Extract > Extract Here
4.  Start a Terminal.
5.  Change to the Folding32 directory.
```
cd /home/arashiko28/Folding32
```
6.  Make the F@H client executable by typing, in the Terminal,
```
chmod +x FAH5-Linux.exe
```
[http://folding.stanford.edu/English/LinConsoleInstall](http://folding.stanford.edu/English/LinConsoleInstall)
7.  Run the client by typing, in the Terminal,
```
./FAH5-Linux.exe
```
8.  The client should start and ask you for some information.
9.  Pick a username to identify yourself.
10.  To join TeamUbuntu, enter 45104 when the client asks you which team to join.
11.  The default choices for the other questions should be correct.

---

### Post by Red Shift on 2008-01-02
> **Pethegreat said:**
> Now I am %60 through a WU. If I stop now to turn off my PC, will all work be for nothing? Or can I resume the WU once I turn my PC back on?
There are times when the WU will not start again if stopped during the middle of a calculation.  I have experienced this ~4 times out of ~60 WUs.  Of course, I did not stop all WUs in mid run.
[quote=arashiko28]Q: Wasn't this supposed to be on the background or as screensaver? I want it as screensaver, but is running from terminal, it just autostarted after the questions.[/quote]
I don't have experience with the screensaver or writing a script to start the F@H client.  There is a how-to on the wiki page.

[http://fahwiki.net/index.php/Running_the_FAH_client_on_Linux](http://fahwiki.net/index.php/Running_the_FAH_client_on_Linux)

### Post by Tundro Walker on 2008-04-04
p2 400mhz + Ubuntu Live CD + Folding@Home = Stupidity in action, or pure awesome?

You be the judge ...

I noticed my brother had some parts laying around, and there was enough to get an old POS p2 400mhz up and running.  I was thinking it might be interesting to ptu this old junk to good use as a low-grade folding client.  

However, 2 catches ...

1) no hard drive
2) BIOS wouldn't boot USB

So, Win95 or 98 were sort of out of the question.  And, the lack of USB boot sort of scrapped ideas for Puppy or DSL linux.  I waffled around for a couple of days researching a solution, and all the answers I was coming up with were overly complex and/or annoying.

However, it had an old cd-rom drive.  So, just for kicks (mostly to laugh at how slow the machine is), I tossed in my Gutsy Ubuntu live cd and booted the thing up.

5 minutes later, it was booted and ready to go.  I was impressed that it actually booted, but more so seeing as how it was functional AND responsive.  Sure, it'd take like 10 seconds for nautilus file browser to come up, but still, not bad for an old granny.  (This things probably 80+ in "dog" years, and like 5000 something in "computer" years)

I had an old 1gb USB flash stick sitting around.  So, I tossed it on there and suddenly had some storage space (no big surprise ... Ubuntu's good about recognizing flash sticks.)

Ubuntu can be finicky with wireless internet, though, but that's all I had access to.  So, on another whim, I stuck a USB wireless adapter I had laying around in the other USB port.  I started messing with the network settings and ... it suddenly had internet connectivity!  (It was the same wireless adapter that my Edgy box was adamant about not using, so I was skeptical about it working, but Gutsy fired it right up!)

Well, no sense in stopping now ... I d/l'ed the folding client, tossed it on the flash stick for storage in case of power outage, and it started grinding away.  I went through and killed off extra processes that weren't needed (update manager, etc) to free up some RAM (got it down to about 80mb of the 384mb on it), and I now have a new slave for the ever-growing army of the undead ... uh, I mean, TeamUbuntu.

In the 3 hours it's been folding, it's already cranked through 8% of a 150,000 Amber project.  :)  It's also raised the ambient temperature in my room about 10 degrees (*cough*). 

As a side note, I still have my Windows computer at work running folding, and recently got a dual-core Windows box to catch up on some modern gaming, which I'm also running the beta SMP client on when not in use.  Both of those machines are also cranking out points for TeamUbuntu.  Talk about p-whipped.  Hey, just because they're running Windows doesn't mean they can't work for us.

Now if only Half-Life 2 and Crysis came out for Linux, I could fully switch over my dual-core box to Linux.  *sigh*

Anwyays, hope you got a laugh out of this.

Viva la revolucion.

---

### Post by Tundro Walker on 2008-04-08
> **Winball said:**
> Ok, 

Im running Hardy Heron 64bit on 2 PC's
E6600, Q6600

When running the SMP client the CPU-cores goes bananas. 
Take a look at the screenshot. 

Anyone know how to solve this?

[IMG]http://79.136.12.154/system-fah.png[/IMG]

EDIT:

I take that back, you're right, that's screwy since you have a quad-core system.  I would have thought each cpu would get maxed all the time.  Maybe their swapping work back and forth?  You might want to also see if there's some other process that's cutting in and interrupting the idle cpu time?  I just don't know, because I mean idle cpu time is idle cpu time, so even though some process has normal priority but only uses 10% cpu, you should still be seeing cpu maxed with 90% getting eaten by the fah.

You're not having heat issues, are you?  You can install a little panel applet called computertemp (I think) which lets you monitor cpu temps.

I'm running the Windows SMP on a dual-core, and it creates 4 threads, too, so I see them bat the cpu time back and forth all the time, but they still add up to maxed out cpu time.  What you have going on is just odd.

~

Also, the SMP client seems to be scoring some crazy points.  I don't know if it's because it's still beta, or what.  I've got the normal client running on 2 2+ghz machines with 1gb RAM each and doing large jobs, and they only avg about 250 points per project.  But my SMP dual core will consistently get 1750 points per project.  It's why I've had such a boost in my "productivity" lately.

(My little p2 400mhz nets 15 points per project...LOL!  It's almost not even worth it, but I love the little under-dog.)

It occurs to me that they should track what kind of comp does the work, so folks can group their work by "weight class", like all the p2's would be a weight class, p3's, etc, and then folks can see how well their individual machines in the weight classes are doing compared to each other, tweaked, overclocked, etc.  

I just know from experience that it's frustrating watching a machine crank out 250 points, thinking it's doing pretty good (which it probably is for it's weight class), then an SMP client comes along and makes it look like a joke.  But, that's because it's apples to oranges, but translated as points, you lose that differentiation.

EDIT (again!):
[URL="http://www.overclock.net/overclock-net-folding-home-team/298558-quad-core-smp-question.html"]
http://www.overclock.net/overclock-net-folding-home-team/298558-quad-core-smp-question.html

[/URL]Some folks at the overclock.net forums noticed the same thing, and attributed it to the beta client perhaps not being fully optimized yet, and/or some overhead in swapping work back and forth between cores.

It's interesting to note one guy on there said he decided to install 3 instances of the client, 2 would use up his quad-cores with 60-80% cpu time on them, and then the third would scrounge off the excess.  LOL!

Maybe you could try that.  Install a second F@H client on each of those quad-core machines using a different comp ID, and let the 2nd one scrounge the spare cpu's.  Man, that'd be insane, but if it worked ...

### Post by Seisen on 2008-04-15
Iis it better to run a dual-core as one processor (smp) or as two seperate processors when folding?

---

### Post by T313C0mun1s7 on 2008-04-15
> **Seisen said:**
> Iis it better to run a dual-core as one processor (smp) or as two seperate processors when folding?

My understanding is that the smp client is designed for quad core and up. This means 4 or more cores, not 2 cores and HyperThreading to make it appear as four cores.

If you want to run on a dual core machine the Stanford FAQs appear to make it sound like it would be better to run two separate instances of the standard client.

The other option is to run the version 6 client with the -smp flag, but I don't know if this is any different from running the smp client. I think they are just merging the clients into one, but they don't say anything about running version 6 with -smp on less than four cores, all they say is that the switch will request smp workunits. So I am not sure what the results would be, of course I  am not aware of any hazards of running the smp core on a dual core, it was just not designed for less than four.

---

### Post by Seisen on 2008-04-15
Well than I will just keep it the way it is than.

---

### Post by Tundro Walker on 2008-04-15
I'm running the SMP beta on my dual-core system.  It creates 4 threads, and they swap %'s back and forth.  Standford wrote in their SMP summary that it's ok to run it on a dual-core, even though it makes 4 threads.

Mine works fine, and the SMP client regularly racks up 1700 pts per work unit.  My dual-core finishes one every 24-36 hours, but the quads seem to crank out a project every 12-15 hours (naturally).

The regular client works on projects that rack up ~300 points max.  So, a dual-core running 2 normal clients would get ~600 points daily vs 1700.  

Personally, I think they're giving too many points for the SMP client, but, hey, if you want min/max your points, you should let your dual-core finish up the wu's it's on, then install the SMP client and try it out.  You can have both versions installed on your machine as long as both aren't running at the same time.  Run a SMP wu, then check out the EOC Folding stats to see if you really got a boost in Points Per Day (PPD).  You should easily see by the daily graph they use.

For instance, I have 2 separate 2+ghz machines running normal clients (at work & home), and they rack up the occasional 250 pts.  Then, when I got my dual-core running the SMP, my scoring jumped dramatically as I was suddenly nailing 1700 pointers.  My dual-core cpu's are 2+ghz themselves, so I would consider them some-what equivalent to the 2 separate 2+ghz comps I got going (other intricacies, like increased bus & ram speeds on the dual-core aside.)

Try it, you might like it.  And try the GPU client while you're at it.  If you're going for points, see which one min/maxes it for you.

---

### Post by Tundro Walker on 2008-04-20
**Quad Core SMP:**

We chatted about that a while back.  Looks like the current client can't utilize all 4 cores to 100% when idle.  Go a few pages back and read the thread.   Should provide some answers.

**Stuck fold:**

I noticed if my Linux client likes to swap back and forth between using the unitinfo.txt file in the /home/folding folder I created for it, and the unitinfo.txt file it created in /home/ one day by itself.  You might want to see if your client is creating files some other place, and you're still looking at the old file, which makes you think nothing's happening.

If worse comes to worse, start up the client in terminal mode IE: instead of just double-clicking on the client to run it from Nautilus (which tends to kick it off in a hidden terminal session, instead open up an actual terminal, go to the folder you have the .exe stored in and kick it off like a shell script ...

```
./FAH504-Linux.exe
```

This should let you see how it's progressing.  If it does indeed look stuck, then CTRL+C to end it.  Next, look for the work unit in the "work" folder (I think) that seems to be the current one stuck, and kick off the folding client with ...

```
./FAH504-Linux.exe -delete X
```

... where X is the work unit to purge.  This should dump that off, and let you download a new wu to work on.

For more help, try googling "folding home delete work unit".  Also, folding client has a decent help file as it is ...

```
./FAH504-Linux.exe -help
```


**As for me...**

### Post by Tundro Walker on 2008-04-24
> **eclark said:**
> haha, yeah. I've got a &quot;research&quot; machine w/ a desk that I have Admin access to in the CS dept so it's cool. I also got two of my other friends to load it on their machines. we completed over 50 WUs for 45104 in two days!!! I'm going to try to convince the lab manager to put it on the image for next year. However, I might have to pitch a Team FU (Furman Universtity) to them to make it happen. I guess it's all going to the same cause, I just wish we could contribute to a Top 100 team ;)

question: I noticed that the SMP client of FAH6 has four instances each running at 96 megs on my machine, although it seems that only one of them is running. Is this normal or do I have it set up wrong. It took me almost two days to complete at 150,000 step WU and when that was done they gave me a 125,000 step WU! Before I installed the SMP client I was doing 500,000 step WU in 12 hours... I feel like this version is slower, or am I mistaken about something? thanks!

50wu's in 2 days?!  Holy cow.  Are you doing small wu's?  I can barely get my 2+ghz machines to crank out a wu every 2 days each, but I've got them set up to do large wu's.

For the SMP thing ... it seems the "step" is a subjective measurement, meaning some project's steps are more intensive than others.  It also depends on the "core" the project uses (Amber, Gromacs, etc).  The SMP projects are generally more labor-intensive.  So, your former projects on the regular client for 150,000 steps are not the same as a 150,000 step SMP project.  Doesn't seem that way, anyways.  That's why the SMP projects score so many more points, like 1400+ as opposed to the 250+ I get on my p4 2+ghz, and also as opposed to the 15+ points I get on the p2 400mhz I've got running stuff.

The regular Linux client is weird in that it'll show like 4 instances of the project in your system monitor, and only one will be using up all the resources.  It's normal, and probably just a nuance of the Linux client, because I haven't seen that same behavior in the Windows client.

The SMP client, however, is setup to thread 4 processes, regardless of whether you use it on a hyper-threading, dual-core or quad-core machine.  It seems to work hyperthreading & dual-core machines the best, maxing out their idle cpu time.  But on quad-cores, it only seems to use ~60% of the total idle cpu.  There's been some discussion of this in past posts, and you can review it for more info.  I think what it came down to for some folks (in other forums I read), is they'd run 2 SMP clients on their quad-core, which would ensure the extra 40-30% of idle cpu time was used, too.  But, check into that before doing it.  The SMP client was intended for 4 core systems, so it's just odd it doesn't make full use of them.

Hope this helps.

---

### Post by gareth_005 on 2008-05-27
> **digital_exhaust said:**
> Thanks.....I'll give it a shot and let you know how it goes.

Hi there, I just joined recently and created a shell script to read the folding status for all my machines into one line each, output looks like this
```
DHARA10 1, 46% [||||______]      May 25 09:40:15 p3408_dpdp-ii
DHARA60 1, 13% [|_________]      May 25 15:55:49 Protein in water
DHARA90 1, 80% [||||||||__]      May 25 15:08:48 p2620_p1475_tet1_03_1 t= 20000.00000
DHARA90 2, 80% [||||||||__]      May 25 15:08:39 p2620_p1475_tet1_03_1 t= 20000.00000

```

I use this line in .conkyrc ```
${font monospace:size=7}${execi 600 sh -c "conkyFah.sh"}${font}
```

I put the shell script is in ~/bin and marked it executable.

p.s. If anyone can tell me how to get this output in a more efficient manner I would be grateful.

```
#!/bin/bash
#
# This script parses a folding at home 'unitinfo.txt' file and prints progress information.
#

# Read the folding status for the specified machine and processor.
#
Display ()
{
	file=$3
	if [ -f $file ]; then
		count=0
		cat $file | while read line; do
			case "$count" in
				0)	count=1
					;;
				1)	count=2
					;;
				2)	#Name
					count=3
					protein=`echo $line | cut -c7-68`
					;;
				3)	#Download time
					count=4
					started=`echo $line | cut -c16-40`
					chars=`echo $started | wc -m`
					padding=""
					while [ $chars -lt 21 ]; do
						chars=$(( $chars + 1 ))
						padding=" $padding"
					done
					started="$padding$started"
					;;
				4)	#Due time
					#required=`echo $line | cut -c11-35`
					count=5
					;;
				5)	#Progress
					count=6
					progress=`echo $line | cut -c11-28`
					chars=`echo $progress | wc -m`
					while [ $chars -lt 17 ]; do
						chars=$(( $chars + 1 ))
						progress=" $progress"
					done
					echo "$1 $2, $progress $started $protein"
					;;
				*)
					;;
			esac
		done
	else
		echo "$1 $2, Status not available"
	fi
}

# Print folding info for all processors if available, otherwise only local.
#
if [ -f /mnt/D0000/.mif ]; then
	Display DHARA10 1 "/mnt/D0000/DHARA10/fah_status_1.txt"
	Display DHARA60 1 "/mnt/D0000/DHARA60/fah_status_1.txt"
	Display DHARA90 1 "/mnt/D0000/DHARA90/fah_status_1.txt"
	Display DHARA90 2 "/mnt/D0000/DHARA90/fah_status_2.txt"
else
	Display DHARA10 1 "/home/gareth/opt/foldingathome/1/unitinfo.txt"
fi

# Done.
#
exit 0

```

---

### Post by Spartan.II.117 on 2008-05-27

### Post by gareth_005 on 2008-05-27
I created a ramdisk on my server machine, 60MB, shared the ramdrive with nfs and mount the share on each machine which needs to communicate stats.

Cron job to copy client stats to the share if it exists every 30 minutes.

Conky then picks up the stats from the shared ramdrive.
I did this to reduce disk writes (Monitored in conky) :)

Ramdrive script:
```
#!/bin/sh
#
# A shell script to create a rem disk.
#

#
#
ramPath=/home/gareth/.ram

# Create the filesystem and media info file.
#   -q Quiet
#   -m Number of reserved blocks.
#
if [ ! -f $ramPath/.mif ]; then
  mke2fs -q -m 0 /dev/ram0
  mount /dev/ram0   $ramPath
  chown root:gareth $ramPath
  chmod 0770        $ramPath
  touch $ramPath/.mif
fi

# Done.
#
exit 0

```

Stats update script:
```
#!/bin/sh
#
# This script copies the folding at home status file 'unitinfo.txt' to the network ram share.
#

# Make sure that the ram disk is valid.
#
if [ -f /mnt/D0000/.mif ]; then
	
	# Make sure that the machine folder exists.
	#
	if [ ! -d /mnt/D0000/DHARA10 ]; then
		mkdir /mnt/D0000/DHARA10
	fi
	
	# Copy the folding at home status file.
	#
	cp /home/gareth/opt/foldingathome/1/unitinfo.txt /mnt/D0000/DHARA10/fah_status_1.txt
fi

# Done.
#
exit 0

```

### Post by gareth_005 on 2008-05-28

> I joined the team today, I'm roughly 26% through my first WU :) 
One quick question though that I haven't been able to find the answer to anywhere...How do I stop the client? I suppose I could just forcibly kill the process, but is there another way? *(Maybe one where it'll quit after the next time it saves it's progress?)*

I'll let it do it's thing during the day but at night I'd like to stop it so I can play some vid's :p


Welcome.

I do all my normal stuff with folding running, P4 with hyperthreading, doesnt seem to hassle my system.

If you installed as a user then probably:
~/opt/foldingathome/foldingathome stop

If you installed as system then probably:
/etc/init.d/foldingathome stop

Other options besides [stop] are [start] and [status]
:)

### Post by jpkotta on 2008-05-28
It really shouldn't affect anything you're trying to do.  I say it's broken if you can't just leave it running all the time because it interfers with other processes.  The 2.6.24.16 kernel in Hardy was misconfigured, and a consequence of that is F@H might take more CPU time than it is supposed to.

### Post by gerapeldoorn2 on 2008-09-01
What is the impact on power consumption?

My quad-core would be a nice folder, but not if I triple my power-bill in the process.

Ger.

---

### Post by freebeer on 2008-09-01
Well, it's not going to triple your power bill. :)

I don't know what the incremental power consumption of an individual core is (and I suppose it varies on the model).  But let's assume that at peak load, a core consumes 50 watts.  Let's also assume that if you're going to leave your machine on anyway, a core at idle consumes 20 watts.  So, per core, you have an incremental consumption of 30 watts.  So 30x4 cores = 120 watts.  1000/120 = 8.33 hours to consume 1 kwh of power.  Or, per day, 2.88 kwh.  if your cost per kwh = $0.10, then it'll add 28.8 cents per day.

One could also factor in the effect of the incremental heat this will produce.  In the cooling season (if your run air conditioning), you'll need to run the a/c just that much longer to remove the additional heat.  In the heating season, the reverse is true... your heating system runs that much less due to the contribution of the heat from the cores.  And so on.

In conclusion... I don't know.  :D

---

### Post by glotz on 2008-09-01

---

### Post by jpkotta on 2008-09-02
> **aaaantoine said:**
> 
if (not nice CPU usage == 0%) and (nice CPU usage > 20%) and (CPU temperature < 65 degrees C), run at full throttle.

You are probably using the kernel's ondemand CPU governor (it's the default).  Look in /sys/devices/system/cpu/cpu0/cpufreq/ondemand/.  There is an entry ignore_nice_load.  Also up_threshold.  I'm pretty sure there is no way to make it look at temperature, unless you coded it yourself.

---

### Post by jpkotta on 2008-10-01
> **computer_freak_8 said:**

```

[20:49:03] + Requesting User ID from server

[20:49:03] -configonly flag given, so exiting.

```

I think that this may be because, when I entered the team ID #, it gave me a "Passkey?" prompt, but I just pressed enter. What is the passkey?

Thanks in advance, 
computer_freak_8

****Edit: Also, when it says "Core Priority (idle/low) [idle]? ", which should I choose? (Which one folds more/less?)****

If you don't know what a passkey is, you don't need to enter one.  It's a way to prevent other people from submitting work as you (personally, if someone wants to submit work as me, I'm all for it).  

idle, the default, is the correct choice, unless the computer is running the F@H client and essentially nothing else.

-configonly just runs the config menu and exits.  Try the -help option.

---

### Post by jpkotta on 2008-11-26
That is an error in ProteinThink.  Contact its author.

It is because the author assumed that an array is always at least 11 elements, which is wrong.  He should have done something like search and replace all "\n" with "" on the bigdata string.

### Post by [BrainBug] on 2008-12-19
If you set it up for Ubuntu 64-bit and install the SMP client you can utilize all of your cores and gain some pretty hefty points per WU.... I'm currently getting quite a few 1920-pt WU's and one machine can pump out 2 or 3 a day on each of my dual quad-core boxes :)

If you're interested I have my SMP client setup instructions written down somewhere.

The only things are that it doesn't install as a service and the cores don't peg the 100% mark.  My cores average out around 60-75% with up and down spikes.

On 11/29 I installed the regular FAH client on each of the boxes and had them use all cores.
On 12/11 I installed Ubuntu 64-bit and the SMP clients.

[http://folding.extremeoverclocking.com/user_summary.php?s=&u=382819](http://folding.extremeoverclocking.com/user_summary.php?s=&u=382819)

[IMG]http://folding.extremeoverclocking.com/graphs/production_day.php?u=382819.jpg[/IMG]

### Post by spiffyjwc on 2008-12-19
Yeah, I can't seem to find out how to get FAH to run on a multi CPU platform to take advantage of all 8 of my cores.  Is there a simple way to do it?  As best as I understand it, i need to have another installation directory "2" where it can launch the other instances....  but I'm not sure how to do it..

---

### Post by [BrainBug] on 2008-12-19
If you have the 64-bit Ubuntu installed this is what I did:

```
sudo apt-get update
mkdir ~/folding
cd ~/folding
wget http://www.stanford.edu/group/pandegroup/folding/release/FAH6.02beta1-Linux.tgz
tar xzf FAH6.02beta1-Linux.tgz
rm fah6
wget http://www.stanford.edu/~kasson/folding/linux/fah6
sudo chmod +x fah6
sudo apt-get install ia32-libs
~/folding/fah6 -smp -configonly
~/folding/fah6 -smp 8 -verbosity 9
```

If you have the standard Ubuntu installed you can run fah_install for the standard client:
[https://help.ubuntu.com/community/FoldingAtHome/fah_install](https://help.ubuntu.com/community/FoldingAtHome/fah_install)

During the setup process it will ask you how many cores. I believe it defaults to 4.  Select 8.  From there it will run a process for each core and peg you at 100% per core.

---

2) If you are into folding, and also a python coder, let me know if you are interested in getting involved. I will not be teaching anyone any python, so this means people who are currently comfortable with the language.

3) At this point, I would ask that you not send requests for new features. I'll get to those once the current lash up is working again.

### Post by capnthommo on 2009-06-01
hi delever
what seems to work for me is (i cant be sure it will for your setup though)
```


~/opt/foldingathome/foldingathome start

~/opt/foldingathome/foldingathome stop

~/opt/foldingathome/foldingathome restart
```

i'm not certain about the restart one because i haven't used it yet but 'start' and 'stop' work for definite - i have used them both - you enter in terminal.
i assume you have fah in your ~/opt folder?  if not then i guess you will have to play with the code a bit.
there is a way to set it up to start on boot but that's beyond me at the moment
anyway, good luck
cheers
nigel

### Post by SoftwareExplorer on 2009-06-09
Hi, this is SoftwareExplorer. I have folded for team 45104 for awhile now and just found this thread. Is there a way to monitor folding at home through the output screenlet?

---

### Post by jpkotta on 2009-06-09
> **SoftwareExplorer said:**
> Hi, this is SoftwareExplorer. I have folded for team 45104 for awhile now and just found this thread. Is there a way to monitor folding at home through the output screenlet?

Probably.  I'm not familiar with screenlets, but Google tells me that this can display the output of an arbitrary command.  Something like ```
tail -f /path/to/FAHlog.txt
``` would probably work.  Where your FAHlog.txt is depends on how you installed F@H.

---

### Post by SoftwareExplorer on 2009-06-14
Thanks. I figured it out before I came back and saw your answer. I did ```
 tail -n 5 /opt/foldingathome/1/FAHlog.txt
``` because the output screenlet renders better with only 5 lines of text.

### Post by SoftwareExplorer on 2009-06-24
I figured out how to monitor FAH from conky. Put```
Folding at Home:
${color red}${execi 15 cat /opt/foldingathome/1/FAHlog.txt | tr '(' '\n' |tr ')' '\n' | grep -E "(%|percent)"|tail -n 1 | tr  -d 'percent'  | tr  -d '%'} %  ${execbar echo "scale=2; $(cat /opt/foldingathome/1/FAHlog.txt | tr '(' '\n' |tr ')' '\n' | grep -E "(%|percent)"|tail -n 1 | tr  -d 'percent'  | tr  -d '%')/100" | bc -q}
```
in your .conkyrc if you used the fah_install script and it should work.

### Post by madailot on 2009-11-12
Wow there are so many replies. What's the different between folding and seti @home?

---

### Post by djchandler on 2009-11-12
> **madailot said:**
> Wow there are so many replies. What's the different between folding and seti @home?

Basically a distributed computing project does about the same thing, one project to the next. You are given a data set to analyze or calculate its permutations, then send the results back to the project.

Seti uses Boinc (Berkeley Open Infrastructure for Network Computing) as its front end, so all you need to do is install it via Synaptic or apt-get, then choose your project. Seti is analyzing data from radio telescopes to look for signs of intelligent  life elsewhere in the universe.

Folding@Home, a project of Stanford University, uses its own client software, and you need to get it from them. But TeamUbuntu can make that a bit easier for you by [starting here]("https://help.ubuntu.com/community/FoldingAtHome"). Installing Origami via Synaptic or apt-get is one option out of 4 known methods. Choose your installation method and join the team. Go to the [Folding@Home index page]("http://folding.stanford.edu/") for the concise and accurate description of the project's goals. Briefly, it's about finding cures for diseases through protein structure analysis and morphing.

---

So, if I set up a virtualbox machine with 8 virtual cores on my 4 core computer, do you think I would get more points?

---

### Post by jpkotta on 2009-11-14
> **SoftwareExplorer said:**
> So, if I set up a virtualbox machine with 8 virtual cores on my 4 core computer, do you think I would get more points?

It depends.  If they scaled the points correctly, then you'll get less points due to the overhead of the VM.  If they made points from 8-core work units "worth more", and the overhead is small enough, then you'll get more points.  In the past they based points on the time it took to do a standard simulation on a reference machine.  So if your machine finished work units in half the time it took the reference machine, you got twice as many ppd as the reference machine.  I haven't looked up what they do to compare the points of a PS3 or GPU to a regular CPU.  

Since the point is to simulate protein folding, you will be better off running without a VM, at least in terms of useful contribution.  I would wager that the overhead of simulating twice as many cores is significant, but the only way to know is to benchmark.

### Post by djchandler on 2009-11-23
Anybody have access to a Windows box besides me? 

I'm now running a notfred implementation of the folding suite on my wife's Windows 7 box. If that Windows machine has more than 1 core, this is a good way to leverage those cores into running smp/A1/A2 core work units. This X2 7750  takes 3 times longer per WU than the Phenom II X4 but it's better than running 1 unit per core under windows in terms of PPD (Windows client won't do SMP yet). Looks like I may pick up as much as 500 ppd this way. YMMV. I'll keep you all posted here.

Notfred runs a busybox implementation of Linux under VMWare Player 3. Administration is through intranet/web interface. Notfred will name the VM and will spill the name and other configuration data on boot. Log in as root only, no password. Make sure you re-configure on the first run through your browser to set up your name, team, and passkey. Reboot can be accomplished via web interface. If you need to configure samba, the text editor is vi, not nano. It's a new (antiquated) experience. Not all busybox commands are available; type help at prompt to list commands, then decipher for yourself.

If you have just two cores, pay close attention to the foldingforum.org topics.

Resources:
Need VMware Player 3
[http://downloads.vmware.com/d/](http://downloads.vmware.com/d/)

Need notfred folding client suite
[http://reilly.homeip.net/folding/vm.html](http://reilly.homeip.net/folding/vm.html)

Additional tips and info
[http://www.hardforum.com/showthread.php?t=1410289](http://www.hardforum.com/showthread.php?t=1410289)
(I'm not using WinAFC-looks like it's running full-tilt to me-you may want it if you need to slow things down)
[http://foldingforum.org/viewtopic.php?f=14&t=12142](http://foldingforum.org/viewtopic.php?f=14&t=12142)
[http://foldingforum.org/viewtopic.php?f=44&t=12011](http://foldingforum.org/viewtopic.php?f=44&t=12011)

### Post by djchandler on 2009-12-01
I'm hoping this is the last word on the stats server issue of 11/11-11/12.

Dr. Pande finally responded in the aforementioned Folding Forum thread discussion (see my previous post, previous page of this thread). If you lost points and have not recovered them, they are indeed lost as far as your points are concerned. WUs were received and the models/calculations are usable that were uploaded during the period in question. The disconnect was at the stats server itself, which apparently experienced a power supply, motherboard, CPU or some similar sort of hardware failure. Therefore the data connection between the uploaded WU and donor was lost. The stats server is now slated for total replacement next month (January 2010).

Because some WUs were at least attributable to a team, they was an attempt to credit the team if not the correct donor. If you didn't get your points you believe you had earned, even if you have logs and WU project, run, clone and generation codes, the data connection was completely broken and no point re-credit is forthcoming.

Be ready for the new stats server to go online in January 2010. In the meantime, watch your logs, track your points and WUs if they're important to you.

Plazzman has re-tasked his Core i7 box apparently.

BTW, [LinuxFanBoi]("http://ubuntuforums.org/member.php?u=714976"), 1500 PPD on a 2.4 Ghz C2D running SMP WUs sounds about right. That's a little less than I'm getting running a notfred client on VMware Player 3.0 (under Windows 7, AMD-V enabled) on a 2.7 ghz Athlon X2 7750. That's a little better than the additional 500 PPD improvement I anticipated over running 2 parallel single core clients under Windows natively. It's taking about 27 hours to complete a 1920 pt. SMP WU, which figures out to about 1700 pts/day. I was barely getting 1000 PPD previously from that box.

---

### Post by jpkotta on 2009-12-25
> **Neezer said:**
> I just installed it on my media server at home...an old p4 but it does have 2gb of ram...

anyways, I am wondering how to check if it is running. I have tried looking at the log, but it seems to be stuck.

```

nathan@server:~$ tail -n 5 /opt/foldingathome/1/FAHlog.txt
[00:00:27] 
[00:00:27] Writing local files
[00:00:27] Extra SSE boost OK.
[00:00:28] Writing local files
[00:00:28] Completed 0 out of 500000 steps  (0%)
You have mail in /var/mail/nathan

```

That is the end of my log...it seems to be stuck on 0 out of 500000.

You can see if it's running with top, htop, or the system monitors that come with KDE or Gnome.  But if it's running and it's been on that step for more than 2 hours, it's broken.  The fix is to reinstall.  Stop the client with ```
/etc/init.d/foldingathome stop
``` and use the installer script with the uninstall option.

---

### Post by djchandler on 2010-03-29
> **Cclips said:**
> Hey guys, I'm trying to figure out the ideal way to setup my origami. I am running it on my laptop (64bit) and at first had it set in its native 32. It was running two processes and had the cpu load maxed out. I was getting about 10% done in an hour or two.

Now though, I installed the 64bit version, which is running 4 processes, and has the cpu pegging around 50-70% load. It also hasn't budged past 1% in an hour or so.

Another curiosity, under 32 bit the stats read CPU 1 and 2, under 64 it just reads one..though I guess that's chopped up to being 1 physical CPU.

Anyway, My question is for a laptop, would it be better to run the 32 bit, or the 64. I noticed the deadline for this one is only 4 days, and at this rate, I don't think that is going to happen on my lil laptop.

Oh, I meant to add that I read up on the 64bit of FAH and that the work for the 64bit was given shorter deadlines and larger work (which explains it taking longer) but I don't get why the CPU load is less under the 64 bit version.

Zelut is the maintainer of the Origami package. Send him a PM if he doesn't respond shortly.

The new 6.29 and 6.24 beta clients are 64-bit only and will download and run SMP WUs, GROMACS CoreA1 through A3, only. If running the 6.29 client and you are getting CoreA3 WUs, you don't want to let those expire. There's a bonus point system in place for those that requires an 80% on-time completion rate. The more quickly you get them done, the more points. Baseline benchmarks are run on an i5 750 system. I'm not sure what client Origami is installing--I do things manually.

The A1 core is older and less efficient. Getting 50-70% CPU usage is normal for core A1. If you go to [http://fah-web.stanford.edu/psummaryC.html](http://fah-web.stanford.edu/psummaryC.html) you can get all the information about which core runs for each WU assigned. [FAH-Addict ]("http://en.fah-addict.net/news/news.php")also has some great information (better than Dr. Pande's blog IMHO).

AFAIK Origami leverages a multi-core CPU by installing multiple clients, one for each detected CPU core, and then specifies each client only downloads uniprocessor WUs. Zelut has the latest info on how Origami works.

I have a laptop and 3 desktops. Only the 3 desktops are folding. I find that the laptop gets way too hot. Whether or not you want to run SMP WUs depends on if you can finish the WUs before the deadline. I certainly would not run the new A3 core on my laptop, which will only work with the 6.29 beta client. The latest version, 2.17, runs fast and hot, even to the point of slowing foreground applications in some people's experience. If I decided to run FAH on a laptop again, I would run the older 6.02 client and specify in the configuration to *not *download WUs using advanced methods. That will probably then only download uniprocessor WUs. Personally I don't like running multiple CPU cores 100% all the time on a laptop. Even running one uniprocessor client, make sure to not enable the CPU affinity lock so the load switches from one core to the other and keeps the heat issues dispersed.

I'm sure someone will come along and disagree with what I say about the laptop. There are things you can do to counteract the problems stated above. You can combat the heat issue by getting a laptop cooler, a tray your laptop sits on and has fans built into it. Those usually run off the USB port, so that raisies battery life issues unless the laptop is plugged into an outlet all the time. Origami installs the FAH client as a service, so it runs at boot. You may want a manual install on the laptop to give you more control over when and how FAH runs.

See our [Wiki ]("https://wiki.ubuntu.com/FoldingAtHomeTeamUbuntu")and [Folding Forum ]("http://foldingforum.org/index.php")if you would like yet more information.

### Post by undecim on 2010-04-21
Easiest way to install:

```
sudo aptitude install origami
sudo origami install -t 45104 -n username
```

If you don't want it scaling up your CPU, then add
```
echo 1 | tee /sys/devices/system/cpu/cpu*/cpufreq/ondemand/ignore_nice_load > /dev/null
``` to /etc/rc.local
and run
```
echo 1 | sudo tee /sys/devices/system/cpu/cpu0/cpufreq/ondemand/ignore_nice_load
```

---

Wow.

Somebody coming out of nowhere like that is not unprecedented. And we have seen cheating incidents before, and we'll probably see them again, the most infamous one being Team FTL . [*That team, in case you are wondering, distributed the FAH client with some  game cracks. Needless to say Stanford did not find this amusing and  zeroed out the whole team's points.*]("http://folding.extremeoverclocking.com/") It's possible this is a [Chimp Challenge]("http://folding.extremeoverclocking.com/chimp_challenge_2010.php") Team entry too, but that started May 5, and that particular team isn't listed. I suppose it is possible to accumulate points like this, as you can now run as many as four 12-core Opterons on a single motherboard, and/or up to four Tesla GPGPU cards. But even that would only get a couple of hundred thousand PPD. Maybe somebody won the Power-Ball or Mega-Millions lottery and decided to put the money to good use.

F@H has a GPU client that is written in a C-like language called CUDA. It is for high performance floating point operations such as protein folding.

It's so much faster than the standard client that I stopped running it so I didn't embarass my Q6700 in front of his 9600GT friends...

---

### Post by NCLI on 2011-01-04
> **t4thfavor said:**
> F@H has a GPU client that is written in a C-like language called CUDA. It is for high performance floating point operations such as protein folding.

It's so much faster than the standard client that I stopped running it so I didn't embarass my Q6700 in front of his 9600GT friends...

### Post by The Real Dave on 2011-01-04
Im folding on my torrent server, a 2.6GHz Celeron, which takes about 1.5 days per WU. I use origami to monitor, and use a little bash script to send the status and temps to a web directory, so I can monitor it without needing to ssh in. I didn't spend more than five minutes on it, so the output isn't very refined :P

Oh, I almost forgot to mention, the reason it takes 1.5 days per WU is because it only folds between 5pm and 8am. I don't want to rocket my electricity bill >.<

```

Celerons aren't likely to increase ur power bill by much; they are predominantly mobile/budget architectures (like my Sempron). Besides, a system like that would probably draw only about 150W at load, so your power bill would rocket by about...... 2 cents. So don't worry about your bill, unless you are overclocking to a large degree :wink:
Hope this helps.

### Post by handy on 2011-01-07
I run a Dell Optiplex GX150, PIII/256MB RAM, 20GB HDD, 24/7 as my standalone headless firewall/router. It rarely spins up the drive & the CPU barely does more than idle.

I measured the electrical power usage of this machine over a period of some days. @ 19 cents a kW it costs $54-/year to run. That is Oz dollars which are about the same as the US dollar these days.

So that gives some idea of the costs. If the CPU was working harder &/or the drive was working it would cost more.

I doubt very much that a Celeron would use less than the PIII 700Mhz.

---

### Post by obscur156 on 2011-01-09
Ok guys,i received my new parts and mounted my new rig.

I have installed my image from the previous machine but Origami is still using 2 cores instead of 6?

Best regards,have a nice day.

---

### Post by jerenept on 2011-01-09
> **obscur156 said:**
> Ok guys,i received my new parts and mounted my new rig.

i have made an image of my old rig with remastersys.
(it was an athlon x2 6400+)

Now i have phenom II x6 1090T clocked at 4017.464 MHz.
I have installed my image from the previous machine but Origami is still using 2 cores instead of 6?

Somebody know what i should do to make origami using my 6 cores ?

Best regards,have a nice day.

you'll have to run ```
sudo origami erase&&sudo origami install -u ~username~ -t 45104.
``` for it to d/l clients for the other cores.
Note: any current folding you are doing will be lost.
P.S. Are you using X64 Ubuntu? I find I get slightly higher PPD"s using the 64-bit client.

---

### Post by obscur156 on 2011-01-09
Ok i will try this imediatly,thanks for your quick reply budy .

Do you think i will have to reboot to make it effective ?

Yes i am using X64 ;-)
Regards

---

### Post by obscur156 on 2011-01-09
Not working because origami already installed,aborting...

---

### Post by jerenept on 2011-01-09
> **obscur156 said:**
> Not working because origami already installed,aborting...

root@obi-System:/home/obi# sudo origami install -u obscur156 -t 45104
ERROR: ORIGAMI APPEARS TO ALREADY BE INSTALLED. ABORTING!

Sorry, I changed the command I posted a minute ago, 'cause I realised you need to remove the current client first. The command to remove is ```
sudo origami erase
```

note: This command will erase any progress you have made on current clients you are running.

### Post by djchandler on 2011-01-10
> **obscur156 said:**
> Looks like we are gonna overtake PlayStation.com Forums Team in about 7 or 8 days \\:D/.

Take care budy .
Regards

And we're being overtaken by 5 more teams within a few months.
[http://folding.extremeoverclocking.com/team_summary.php?s=&t=45104](http://folding.extremeoverclocking.com/team_summary.php?s=&t=45104)

Our points are down from our top production from about a year ago.
[http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=8644195&postcount=1325](http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=8644195&postcount=1325)

I realize there have been some problems running F@H on 10,10, but why not run SMP work units instead of multiple instances of the classic client? The points for A3 SMP WUs are far more than what you can get running even 6 instances on your Phenom II X6. I'm getting ~3300 points for some WUs done in 7.5 hours (60xx projects) or ~5600 points in 15.5 hours for 6701 or 6702 WUs. This is on a Phenom II X6 1090T with an easy overclock to 3.6 Ghz (stock at 3.2).

[https://help.ubuntu.com/community/FoldingAtHome/ManualInstall](https://help.ubuntu.com/community/FoldingAtHome/ManualInstall)

I'm taking one for the team by cheating a bit, running the Windows 6.30 client natively. (My wife and I are doing a Windows 7/Office 2010/Sharepoint project.) You can do this also using WINE or in a virtual Windows machine, and it doesn't require 64-bit Linux.

Here is a work-around discussion for the Linux 64-bit client.
[http://foldingforum.org/viewtopic.php?f=44&t=16447](http://foldingforum.org/viewtopic.php?f=44&t=16447)
[http://foldingforum.org/viewtopic.php?f=58&t=14782#p145834](http://foldingforum.org/viewtopic.php?f=58&t=14782#p145834)

CORRECTION: I'm getting these units done in under **6.5** hours, including upload. I'm still trying to understand why some WUs, such as the 67XXs, seem to penalize, and if it's only on AMD CPUs that this is happening.

### Post by The Real Dave on 2011-01-12
> **jerenept said:**
> Celerons aren't likely to increase ur power bill by much; they are predominantly mobile/budget architectures (like my Sempron). Besides, a system like that would probably draw only about 150W at load, so your power bill would rocket by about...... 2 cents. So don't worry about your bill, unless you are overclocking to a large degree :wink:
Hope this helps.

No, they're not that powerful, but seeing as I plan on folding for the foreseeable future, even a small saving a year is a big thing. Going by your estimation of 150W, running flat out 365.4 days a year, would work out as,

```
.15kW x 8769.6Hours/Year = 1315.44kWH/Year @ €0.1325/kWH = €174.30/Year
```

That's a lot of money >.<

Instead, look at it running for 15 Hours a day,

```
.15kW x 5481Hours/Year = 822.15kWH/Year @ €0.1325/kWH = €109/Year
```

That's a saving of €65.30/Year, whilst still doing my bit.

> **handy said:**
> I run a Dell Optiplex GX150, PIII/256MB RAM, 20GB HDD, 24/7 as my standalone headless firewall/router. It rarely spins up the drive & the CPU barely does more than idle.

I measured the electrical power usage of this machine over a period of some days. @ 19 cents a kW it costs $54-/year to run. That is Oz dollars which are about the same as the US dollar these days.

So that gives some idea of the costs. If the CPU was working harder &/or the drive was working it would cost more.

I doubt very much that a Celeron would use less than the PIII 700Mhz.

Very true, as the above calculations show >.< I used use a PIII Katami @ 451Mhz as my main server once upon a time, running FreeNAS :)


Also, I've managed to convince my school's IT guy to allow me to run F@H on a few school machines, C2Ds OCd to 3.2Ghz. I've four of these machines running, but as of yet, they havn't uploaded a single WU, which makes me think something's gone wrong. :( Must have a look at them.

### Post by jerenept on 2011-01-12
> **koven said:**
> hey guys..im having some trouble with FAH 6.30 and HFM 0.6.1.251

Can't help you dude, it seems to be a bug in either mono or HFM's code. There is another monitoring application you could use, which has served me well. It's called [FAHMON]('http://fahmon.net/download.html'), but it needs to be compiled... Anyway, all HFM and other apps like it do are monitor F@H's progress; they do not have any effect on the speed of completing Work Units, or your Points Per Day.

---

### Post by djchandler on 2011-01-15
> **obscur156 said:**
> Hi guys, i am having a problem with Origami since i have changed my Pc.
Now i have a  AMD PHENOM 2 x6 1090t.

When i have a WU (working unit) finished , it looks like its not uploading the results and not downloading new WU and can accumulate multiple WU's at 100%...

I have to reboot to make it upload the results and downloading new WU's.

I am running maverick 64 bit and origami (0.7.4) from the repo.

Anyone have a clue ?

Regards

You can check the status of the server that you are uploading results to at
[http://fah-web.stanford.edu/serverstat.html](http://fah-web.stanford.edu/serverstat.html)
Sometimes servers are down for maintenance or other issues.

You can also check for issues with a specific server at
[http://foldingforum.org/viewforum.php?f=18](http://foldingforum.org/viewforum.php?f=18)

If the problem is on your end, it could be an issue with your internet connection. Results are uploaded using http; it's not a firewall problem.

Results can be manually forced to upload by manually stopping the client, and manually running each instance you have installed.
./fah6 -sendall
will send all results and exit.

IMHO, one of the problems with installing with origami or the finstall script is making fah a service running in the background. This removes your direct control of each client, i.e., no terminal window. As a service, the only reliable way I know of to stop your clients without risking losing data is what you're doing, re-booting.

Look at alternative install methods listed at
[https://help.ubuntu.com/community/FoldingAtHome](https://help.ubuntu.com/community/FoldingAtHome)

Maybe one of those will suit your needs better than origami, if not for the purpose of using the -smp flag, then for the purpose of finer control of the client(s).

BTW, Ubuntu isn't the only distribution having issues with running F@H. The problem appears to be in the kernel. I may try running a Linux client (Ubuntu 10.04 AMD64) on my hexacore to see if I encounter the some of the problem(s) others are.

---

---

### Post by djchandler on 2011-01-16
> **obscur156 said:**
> ...so maybe its only having problem to download new WU's.

Sometimes i have to reboot and sometimes just stoping and restarting Origami will do the job for downloading new WU's

Hoping to find the problem.
Regards
That can happen when there's no more work to do for the moment. The servers can periodically run out of work units when running the uniprocessor client.

On the other hand, there never seems to be a shortage of WUs available from certain project leaders. I have never run out of work to do on any projects run by Kasson. Coincidentally, those are almost all the experimental GROMACS A3 and A4 WUs, otherwise known as SMP2 (-advmethods plus a passkey), which require multiple processing threads (-SMP). There are bonuses for quick turnarounds for those. The research being done with those WUs applies to computer science as well as molecular biology.

Projects
[http://fah-web.stanford.edu/psummary.html](http://fah-web.stanford.edu/psummary.html)

Points Calculator
[http://www.linuxforge.net/bonuscalc2.php](http://www.linuxforge.net/bonuscalc2.php)

Projects 2684-2692 (-bigadv) require 8 threads and 8 GB of RAM; Servers or workstations with multiple CPUs totaling at least 8 cores, Intel i7 (4 cores x 2 threads per core by enabling hyperthreading) or AMD Opteron Magny-cours CPUs (8+ cores) are required for those.

[Grandpa_01's chart ]("http://foldingforum.org/viewtopic.php?p=131077#p131077")in this thread posted February 2010 helps define what is required. There are no magny-cours CPUs listed as the list was compiled before their release in March 2010. Intel Sandy Bridge CPUs were just released a week and a half ago.
[http://foldingforum.org/viewtopic.php?p=131077#p131077](http://foldingforum.org/viewtopic.php?p=131077#p131077)

If you want the big points for the experimental WUs, read the [Quick Return Bonus Plan Qualification ]("http://foldingforum.org/viewtopic.php?f=58&t=13160")post on Folding Forum. The baseline is established by benchmarks on an i5 750 desktop system. There's no documentation I can find on how the -bigadv units are actually baselined.

---

### Post by ubiquitin.jf on 2012-01-07
I don't even know where to begin with that attitude.

Anyway, if anyone fancies a more interactive way to contribute to human knowledge, I can wholeheartedly recommend Foldit. It's a frontend to the Rosetta@home project (which predicts and refines models of fully folded proteins, rather than how they fold) which takes the form of a competitive game where players fit proteins into energetically favorable conformations. No knowledge of molecular biology required!

My guess is that Origami stores work in /var/lib/origami/foldingathome/CPU1/work  so if my Windows install points to that via symlink or whatever (hang on do these exist in W7) with the correct permissions, I can work the same unit no matter what OS I'm running?

---

### Post by jerenept on 2012-03-03
> **Mojosdad said:**
> I used to fold some time ago, and have re-discovered this project. I've installed FAH via Origami, but unfortunately my machine splits its time between Linux and Windows 7. Is there and easy way to share the WU folder between the dual boots.

My guess is that Origami stores work in /var/lib/origami/foldingathome/CPU1/work  so if my Windows install points to that via symlink or whatever (hang on do these exist in W7) with the correct permissions, I can work the same unit no matter what OS I'm running?

You should not do that, as the Windows and Linux clients are different enough that doing this may cause some serious problems. If you can do the units fast enough that they don't expire, I see no problem in dividing your time between W7 and Ubuntu.

### Post by NacIK on 2012-03-05
> **Mojosdad said:**
> I used to fold some time ago, and have re-discovered this project. I've installed FAH via Origami, but unfortunately my machine splits its time between Linux and Windows 7. Is there and easy way to share the WU folder between the dual boots.

I have Windows 7 running under VirtualBox.  This prevents me from having to reboot my computer all the time and it makes it easier to share files.  Anyone still dual-booting and not a "hardcore gamer" should look into VirtualBox.  Both systems stay up and running 24/7 and work flawlessly.

### Post by T313C0mun1s7 on 2012-03-24
Yea, the nice thing about the Core i7 and nVidia Optimist graphics combo is that (*under Windows, which because of my business I had to go back to*) the GPU only kicks in for individual apps that require it. Everything else runs off the i7 integrated graphics. Since Optimist allows for an **app by app** selection of the GPU in use, for most things (except gaming, Photoshop, Google Earth, etc.) my GPU client still has the full GPU to itself, even when I am using the computer. Most programs and desktop composting is done entirely by the integrated GPU in the i7.

### Post by T313C0mun1s7 on 2012-03-25
> **BertN45 said:**
> I came across this thread and 3 of my old PCs are now contributing:
- AMD Athlon 64 3200+  with Ubuntu 12.04
- Pentium IV 3.2 gHz   with Ubuntu 12.04
- Pentium III 650 mHz  with Windows XP

I wonder if the last one gets any work done within a reasonable due time. All processors are on 24/7.

I still consider my laptop, but that one is almost always off and a 486 66mHz 16MB with WfW 3.11, but that one is more for the museum.

Welcome aboard.

The PIII will get some work done, as long as you are not requesting large work units or anything from the scientific (beta) core. Expect it to take several days to get a work unit done, but if you leave it alone and let it fold all the time it should get them turned in before the deadline. If it has trouble getting WUs in on time you can try finding the older version 504 of the console client. Provided there is any work left on the Fahcore 78 the old client will pick those up and you will have a two week deadline. Also, if you opt to use the version 504 console client, which is a good idea for older hardware, then use the -forceasm switch as well. It is now almost essential to force legacy work units with that client, and that is what the flag will do for you.

---

### Post by Hedgehog1 on 2012-07-11
Well, I have been running F@H for 5 weeks now, and have passed the million point mark a few days ago.

Figuring out how points are calculated is very odd - the same bank of computers get widely different numbers depending on the work units in the queue that day.

On July 9th I did 24 work units, and got 74,939 points that day.
On July 10th I did 25 work units, and got 53,366 points that day.

Same systems, all working 24/7.  I guess that averaging points per day is the best way to see your true net output.

On a side note - Does anyone know who "Dr._Alexi_Zarkov" really is?  He/She has been pumping out points like crazy.  I am curious as to the hardware being used.

***The Hedge***

:KS

p.s. I am converting my F@H systems over to 'cube' computers. The Shuttle SH67H3 has a 'cube-ish' case, mother board, power supply and nice ICE cooling.  I add an i7 2700K CPU and 8 gigs of ram (cause it cost about the same as 4 gigs of ram).  

The i7 2700K just about matches my six core AMD black CPU (The AMD CPU is no longer available, sadly).  Both systems are Ubuntu 12.04 and each pump out about 22,000 points a day.  I also have two windows systems with 4-core i5 processors, and these each produce about 11,000 points per day.

I like that the Shuttle units can stack, and don't build up heat inside at all.  They do warm the room - but any CPU running at 100% 24/7 is going to do that.

### Post by spikku on 2012-07-13
After all the work I've recently done on my folding stuff, I thought I'd finally stop by and say hi.

Hi!

So, I've been folding for TeamUbuntu since last September (BoAllen). I was doing very well in the charts for awhile until Dr. Alexi and Hedgehog came and pwnd me. >.<

(Nice work!)

A couple of tidbits to share:

**Tidbit 1:**
I recently added a GTX460. It was awesome, and upped my PPD by about 13k! Well, all of a sudden, it just stopped working. It went down to 400 PPD. After a bunch of unsuccessful trying-to-figure-it-out, I finally found the problem. Turn off Windows XP screen saver... Back to 13k PPD.

**Tidbit 2:**
I have two identical CPU/SMP setups (Phenom X6). One is dedicated (not used for other things), and gets about 11k PPD. The other is my workstation. I use it for web development, games, etc. for 3-4 hours a day. It's always folding on six cores (I don't really notice an impact on my work), and it gets about 8k PPD.

**Tidbit 3:**
I just got HFM setup. I *highly* recommend it for serious folders with multiple machines, GPUs, etc.
[http://code.google.com/p/hfm-net/](http://code.google.com/p/hfm-net/)
I can monitor all of my SMP and GPU folding, across different servers and networks. HFM can pull your data from an FTP server, so here's what I do:
I have an FTP account with different folders for my different SMP/GPU instances (i.e., /home1SMP, /home1GPU, etc.). If you don't have an FTP server, I think this would work with a free drivehq.com account because the Python FTP update script I wrote never logs out of the FTP account (I initially used drivehq.com but got locked out because the original Python script would reconnect every 15 minutes, and free accounts have a login limit...). Here's the Python script:

```

#!/usr/bin/python

import os
from ftplib import FTP
from time import gmtime, strftime, sleep

# CONFIG FTP
ftp_host = 'ftp.server.com'
ftp_user = 'jsmith'
ftp_pass = 'f46g23478fgnc8g845'
ftp_folder = 'server1SMP'
update_minutes = ["00", "15", "30", "45"]

# CONFIG FILES
files = []
files.append('/home/jsmith/folding/FAHlog.txt')
files.append('/home/jsmith/folding/queue.dat')
files.append('/home/jsmith/folding/unitinfo.txt')

def upload(ftp, remote, local):
    ext = os.path.splitext(local)[1]
    if ext in (".txt", ".htm", ".html"):
        ftp.storlines("STOR " + remote, open(local))
    else:
        ftp.storbinary("STOR " + remote, open(local, "rb"), 1024)

ftp = FTP(ftp_host)
ftp.login(ftp_user, ftp_pass)
ftp.cwd(ftp_folder)
print "CWD " + ftp.pwd()

while (True):
    minute = strftime("%M", gmtime())
    if minute in update_minutes:
        for local in files:
            remote = local[local.rfind('/')+1:]
            print "STOR %s" % remote
            upload(ftp, remote, local)
        print "--------"
    ftp.sendcmd("NOOP")
    print "NOOP"
    sleep(60)

ftp.quit()

```

Maybe it will help. :D

### Post by Hedgehog1 on 2012-08-01
My setup is pretty simple right now.

My server farm is based on units like this:

SHUTTLE SH67H3 PC Barebone System
i7 2700k
8 gigs ram (it costs about the same as smaller sizes of ram)

They boot from:
ADATA Superior Series S102 Pro 16GB USB 3.0 Flash Drive.

The flash drive is in a USB 2.0 socket, as Linux cannot boot from USB 3.0 sockets yet.  But it is fast, cheap and easy to replicate.

These units are small, quiet and stack-able. I run them headless, but did load telnetd so I can connect to them and reboot/powerdown them if needed.

For now I just have them added to my wired network and monitor them from my main Ubuntu PC using FAHControl.  FAHControl allows you to add systems to monitor.

My goal is to have 8-10 of these shuttle units humming away doing FAH.  Right now I am at three.  My other 3 systems are my main Ubuntu system (AMD 6 core box) and two windows i5 based units that produce about the same points as one Shuttle/i7 box.  I will be phasing the windows system out of FAH once I have the full number of Shuttle based units running Ubuntu.

I just packed up what would have been unit #4 for a swap - the first two DIMM slots were not responding.  Amazon is sending a replacement.

I chose the Shuttle based farm because they are reasonably inexpensive to build, and can be used as real desktops if that is ever needed.  Their design draws very little power.

So far my only complaint has been 2 out of 5 units sent to me had a mother board issue.  Amazon is great at swapping out a unit and picking up the bad one for free; but based on the reviews I think the 'bad board' rate is normally much lower.  Once I have 8-10 running I will know for sure.

They sure look pretty, anyway!

***The Hedge***

:KS

---

### Post by Hedgehog1 on 2012-08-01
Just a note on preparing the USB sticks:

First I load Ubuntu 12.04 on one and get it setup just the way I like it.  Then I make a copy of the USB stick using the dd command.

From my main system, the command to make an image of a USB stick looks like this:

```
sudo dd bs=1M if=/dev/sdg of=/home/marc/Folding/shuttle8.img
```

I then make new USB sticks by writing the 'img' to a new USB stick:

```
sudo dd bs=1M if=/home/marc/Folding/shuttle8.img of=/dev/sdg
```

The I boot the new USB stick on a shuttle box with the network disconnected and change the units name in two places:

```
sudo gedit /etc/hosts

sudo gedit /etc/hostname
```

After a reboot, the box knows its new name and is ready to go.

***The Hedge***

:KS

p.s. My USB sticks start at '/dev/sdg' - your will likely be a different letter('/dev/sdd' or '/dev/sde').  Make sure you use the correct '/dev/sd**X**'.  You can mess up your system if you try to overwrite your hard drive by using the wrong '/dev/sd**X**' value.

### Post by Hedgehog1 on 2012-09-09
I think that if you had been using a $600 GPU, you might have seen a better GPU output and missed the performance.

However, each of my i7 server farm units cost $600 total and pump output 18-24k ppd each (depends on the work units each day).

I have the 'big' $600 GPU in my main Ubuntu system, and therefore have the bigger case, lots of fans and huge power supply.  I don't use the GPU for FAH (the 6 core AMD does that FAH work on this unit).  If I had to do it over again, I would not have moved up to such a big GPU.

Frankly a PS3 or Xbox are better bang for the video game buck.

I may play with CUDA programming on it someday, but it has a limited feature set compared to CPU based programming.

***The Hedge***

:KS

p.s. The AMD system has a simple water cooling system on the AMD 6 core (from Antec) that works a treat.

The six shuttle based servers in my farm are using the air cooling that comes with the Shuttle cases (They call it ICS) and it works fine.  They have been running 24/7 without a hiccup yet.  If they work for that first hour at 100% load, they seem to just keep running without complaint forever after that.
